3518     * StringUtils.isAsciiPrintable("ab2c")   = true
3519     * StringUtils.isAsciiPrintable("!ab-c~") = true
3520     * StringUtils.isAsciiPrintable("\u0020") = true
3521     * StringUtils.isAsciiPrintable("\u0021") = true
3522     * StringUtils.isAsciiPrintable("\u007e") = true
3523     * StringUtils.isAsciiPrintable("\u007f") = false
3524     * StringUtils.isAsciiPrintable("Ceki G\u00fclc\u00fc") = false
3525     * </pre>
3526     *
3527     * @param cs the CharSequence to check, may be null
3528     * @return {@code true} if every character is in the range
3529     *  32 through 126
3530     * @since 2.1
3531     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from isAsciiPrintable(String) to isAsciiPrintable(CharSequence)
3532     */
3533    public static boolean isAsciiPrintable(final CharSequence cs) {
3534        if (cs == null) {
3535            return false;
3536        }
3537        final int sz = cs.length();
3538        for (int i = 0; i < sz; i++) {
3539            if (!CharUtils.isAsciiPrintable(cs.charAt(i))) {
3540                return false;
3541            }
3542        }
3543        return true;

3546    /**
3547     * Checks if a CharSequence is empty (""), null or whitespace only.
3548     *
3549     * <p>Whitespace is defined by {@link Character#isWhitespace(char)}.</p>
3550     *
3551     * <pre>
3552     * StringUtils.isBlank(null)      = true
3553     * StringUtils.isBlank("")        = true
3554     * StringUtils.isBlank(" ")       = true
3555     * StringUtils.isBlank("bob")     = false
3556     * StringUtils.isBlank("  bob  ") = false
3557     * </pre>
3558     *
3559     * @param cs  the CharSequence to check, may be null
3560     * @return {@code true} if the CharSequence is null, empty or whitespace only
3561     * @since 2.0
3562     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from isBlank(String) to isBlank(CharSequence)
3563     */
3564    public static boolean isBlank(final CharSequence cs) {
3565        final int strLen = length(cs);
3566        if (strLen == 0) {
3567            return true;
3568        }
3569        for (int i = 0; i < strLen; i++) {
3570            if (!Character.isWhitespace(cs.charAt(i))) {
3571                return false;
3572            }
3573        }
3574        return true;
3575    }

3577    /**
3578     * Checks if a CharSequence is empty ("") or null.
3579     *
3580     * <pre>
3581     * StringUtils.isEmpty(null)      = true
3582     * StringUtils.isEmpty("")        = true
3583     * StringUtils.isEmpty(" ")       = false
3584     * StringUtils.isEmpty("bob")     = false
3585     * StringUtils.isEmpty("  bob  ") = false
3586     * </pre>
3587     *
3588     * <p>NOTE: This method changed in Lang version 2.0.
3589     * It no longer trims the CharSequence.
3590     * That functionality is available in isBlank().</p>
3591     *
3592     * @param cs  the CharSequence to check, may be null
3593     * @return {@code true} if the CharSequence is empty or null
3594     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from isEmpty(String) to isEmpty(CharSequence)
3595     */
3596    public static boolean isEmpty(final CharSequence cs) {
3597        return cs == null || cs.length() == 0;
3598    }

3600    /**
3601     * Checks if the CharSequence contains mixed casing of both uppercase and lowercase characters.
3602     *
3603     * <p>{@code null} will return {@code false}. An empty CharSequence ({@code length()=0}) will return
3604     * {@code false}.</p>
3605     *
3606     * <pre>
3607     * StringUtils.isMixedCase(null)    = false
3608     * StringUtils.isMixedCase("")      = false
3609     * StringUtils.isMixedCase(" ")     = false
3610     * StringUtils.isMixedCase("ABC")   = false
3611     * StringUtils.isMixedCase("abc")   = false
3612     * StringUtils.isMixedCase("aBc")   = true
3613     * StringUtils.isMixedCase("A c")   = true
3614     * StringUtils.isMixedCase("A1c")   = true
3615     * StringUtils.isMixedCase("a/C")   = true
3616     * StringUtils.isMixedCase("aC\t")  = true
3617     * </pre>
3618     *
3619     * @param cs the CharSequence to check, may be null
3620     * @return {@code true} if the CharSequence contains both uppercase and lowercase characters
3621     * @since 3.5
3622     */
3623    public static boolean isMixedCase(final CharSequence cs) {
3624        if (isEmpty(cs) || cs.length() == 1) {
3625            return false;
3626        }
3627        boolean containsUppercase = false;
3628        boolean containsLowercase = false;
3629        final int sz = cs.length();
3630        for (int i = 0; i < sz; i++) {
3631            char nowChar = cs.charAt(i);
3632            if (Character.isUpperCase(nowChar)) {
3633                containsUppercase = true;
3634            } else if (Character.isLowerCase(nowChar)) {
3635                containsLowercase = true;
3636            }
3637            if (containsUppercase && containsLowercase) {
3638                return true;
3639            }
3640        }
3641        return false;
3642    }

3659     * StringUtils.isNoneBlank(new String[]{""}) = false

3737    /**
3738     * Checks if the CharSequence contains only Unicode digits.
3739     * A decimal point is not a Unicode digit and returns false.
3740     *
3741     * <p>{@code null} will return {@code false}.
3742     * An empty CharSequence (length()=0) will return {@code false}.</p>
3743     *
3744     * <p>Note that the method does not allow for a leading sign, either positive or negative.
3745     * Also, if a String passes the numeric test, it may still generate a NumberFormatException
3746     * when parsed by Integer.parseInt or Long.parseLong, e.g. if the value is outside the range
3747     * for int or long respectively.</p>
3748     *
3749     * <pre>
3750     * StringUtils.isNumeric(null)   = false
3751     * StringUtils.isNumeric("")     = false
3752     * StringUtils.isNumeric("  ")   = false
3753     * StringUtils.isNumeric("123")  = true
3754     * StringUtils.isNumeric("\u0967\u0968\u0969")  = true
3755     * StringUtils.isNumeric("12 3") = false
3756     * StringUtils.isNumeric("ab2c") = false
3757     * StringUtils.isNumeric("12-3") = false
3758     * StringUtils.isNumeric("12.3") = false
3759     * StringUtils.isNumeric("-123") = false
3760     * StringUtils.isNumeric("+123") = false
3761     * </pre>
3762     *
3763     * @param cs  the CharSequence to check, may be null
3764     * @return {@code true} if only contains digits, and is non-null
3765     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from isNumeric(String) to isNumeric(CharSequence)
3766     * @since 3.0 Changed "" to return false and not true
3767     */
3768    public static boolean isNumeric(final CharSequence cs) {
3769        if (isEmpty(cs)) {
3770            return false;
3771        }
3772        final int sz = cs.length();
3773        for (int i = 0; i < sz; i++) {
3774            if (!Character.isDigit(cs.charAt(i))) {
3775                return false;
3776            }
3777        }
3778        return true;
3779    }
3780
3781    /**
3782     * Checks if the CharSequence contains only Unicode digits or space
3783     * ({@code ' '}).
3784     * A decimal point is not a Unicode digit and returns false.
3785     *
3786     * <p>{@code null} will return {@code false}.
3787     * An empty CharSequence (length()=0) will return {@code true}.</p>
3788     *
3789     * <pre>
3790     * StringUtils.isNumericSpace(null)   = false
3791     * StringUtils.isNumericSpace("")     = true
3792     * StringUtils.isNumericSpace("  ")   = true
3793     * StringUtils.isNumericSpace("123")  = true
3794     * StringUtils.isNumericSpace("12 3") = true
3795     * StringUtils.isNumericSpace("\u0967\u0968\u0969")  = true
3796     * StringUtils.isNumericSpace("\u0967\u0968 \u0969")  = true
3797     * StringUtils.isNumericSpace("ab2c") = false
3798     * StringUtils.isNumericSpace("12-3") = false
3799     * StringUtils.isNumericSpace("12.3") = false
3800     * </pre>
3801     *
3802     * @param cs  the CharSequence to check, may be null
3803     * @return {@code true} if only contains digits or space,
3804     *  and is non-null
3805     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from isNumericSpace(String) to isNumericSpace(CharSequence)
3806     */
3807    public static boolean isNumericSpace(final CharSequence cs) {
3808        if (cs == null) {
3809            return false;
3810        }
3811        final int sz = cs.length();
3812        for (int i = 0; i < sz; i++) {
3813            final char nowChar = cs.charAt(i);
3814            if (nowChar != ' ' && !Character.isDigit(nowChar)) {
3815                return false;
3816            }
3817        }
3818        return true;
3819    }
3820
3821    /**
3822     * Checks if the CharSequence contains only whitespace.
3823     *
3824     * <p>Whitespace is defined by {@link Character#isWhitespace(char)}.</p>
3825     *
3826     * <p>{@code null} will return {@code false}.
3827     * An empty CharSequence (length()=0) will return {@code true}.</p>
3828     *
3829     * <pre>
3830     * StringUtils.isWhitespace(null)   = false
3831     * StringUtils.isWhitespace("")     = true
3832     * StringUtils.isWhitespace("  ")   = true
3833     * StringUtils.isWhitespace("abc")  = false
3834     * StringUtils.isWhitespace("ab2c") = false
3835     * StringUtils.isWhitespace("ab-c") = false
3836     * </pre>
3837     *
3838     * @param cs  the CharSequence to check, may be null
3839     * @return {@code true} if only contains whitespace, and is non-null
3840     * @since 2.0
3841     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from isWhitespace(String) to isWhitespace(CharSequence)
3842     */
3843    public static boolean isWhitespace(final CharSequence cs) {
3844        if (cs == null) {
3845            return false;
3846        }
3847        final int sz = cs.length();
3848        for (int i = 0; i < sz; i++) {
3849            if (!Character.isWhitespace(cs.charAt(i))) {
3850                return false;
3851            }
3852        }
3853        return true;
3854    }

3856    /**
3857     * Joins the elements of the provided array into a single String containing the provided list of elements.
3858     *
3859     * <p>
3860     * No delimiter is added before or after the list. Null objects or empty strings within the array are represented
3861     * by empty strings.
3862     * </p>
3863     *
3864     * <pre>
3865     * StringUtils.join(null, *)              = null
3866     * StringUtils.join([], *)                = ""
3867     * StringUtils.join([null], *)            = ""
3868     * StringUtils.join([false, false], ';')  = "false;false"
3869     * </pre>
3870     *
3871     * @param array
3872     *            the array of values to join together, may be null
3873     * @param delimiter
3874     *            the separator character to use
3875     * @return the joined String, {@code null} if null array input
3876     * @since 3.12.0
3877     */
3878    public static String join(final boolean[] array, final char delimiter) {
3879        if (array == null) {
3880            return null;
3881        }
3882        return join(array, delimiter, 0, array.length);
3883    }

3885    /**
3886     * Joins the elements of the provided array into a single String containing the provided list of elements.
3887     *
3888     * <p>
3889     * No delimiter is added before or after the list. Null objects or empty strings within the array are represented
3890     * by empty strings.
3891     * </p>
3892     *
3893     * <pre>
3894     * StringUtils.join(null, *)                   = null
3895     * StringUtils.join([], *)                     = ""
3896     * StringUtils.join([null], *)                 = ""
3897     * StringUtils.join([true, false, true], ';')  = "true;false;true"
3898     * </pre>
3899     *
3900     * @param array
3901     *            the array of values to join together, may be null
3902     * @param delimiter
3903     *            the separator character to use
3904     * @param startIndex
3905     *            the first index to start joining from. It is an error to pass in a start index past the end of the
3906     *            array
3907     * @param endIndex
3908     *            the index to stop joining from (exclusive). It is an error to pass in an end index past the end of
3909     *            the array
3910     * @return the joined String, {@code null} if null array input
3911     * @since 3.12.0
3912     */
3913    public static String join(final boolean[] array, final char delimiter, final int startIndex, final int endIndex) {
3914        if (array == null) {
3915            return null;
3916        }
3917        if (endIndex - startIndex <= 0) {
3918            return EMPTY;
3919        }
3920        final StringBuilder stringBuilder = new StringBuilder(array.length * 5 + array.length - 1);
3921        for (int i = startIndex; i < endIndex; i++) {
3922            stringBuilder
3923                    .append(array[i])
3924                    .append(delimiter);
3925        }
3926        return stringBuilder.substring(0, stringBuilder.length() - 1);
3927    }

4331     * @param iterable  the {@link Iterable} providing the values to join together, may be null

4340    /**
4341     * Joins the elements of the provided {@link Iterator} into
4342     * a single String containing the provided elements.
4343     *
4344     * <p>No delimiter is added before or after the list. Null objects or empty
4345     * strings within the iteration are represented by empty strings.</p>
4346     *
4347     * <p>See the examples here: {@link #join(Object[],char)}.</p>
4348     *
4349     * @param iterator  the {@link Iterator} of values to join together, may be null
4350     * @param separator  the separator character to use
4351     * @return the joined String, {@code null} if null iterator input
4352     * @since 2.0
4353     */
4354    public static String join(final Iterator<?> iterator, final char separator) {
4355        // handle null, zero and one elements before building a buffer
4356        if (iterator == null) {
4357            return null;
4358        }
4359        if (!iterator.hasNext()) {
4360            return EMPTY;
4361        }
4362        return Streams.of(iterator).collect(LangCollectors.joining(toStringOrEmpty(String.valueOf(separator)), EMPTY, EMPTY, StringUtils::toStringOrEmpty));
4363    }
4364

4366     * Joins the elements of the provided {@link Iterator} into

4370     * A {@code null} separator is the same as an empty String ("").</p>

4373     *

4375     * @param separator  the separator character to use, null treated as ""
4376     * @return the joined String, {@code null} if null iterator input
4377     */
4378    public static String join(final Iterator<?> iterator, final String separator) {
4379        // handle null, zero and one elements before building a buffer
4380        if (iterator == null) {
4381            return null;
4382        }
4383        if (!iterator.hasNext()) {
4384            return EMPTY;
4385        }
4386        return Streams.of(iterator).collect(LangCollectors.joining(toStringOrEmpty(separator), EMPTY, EMPTY, StringUtils::toStringOrEmpty));
4387    }
4388
4389    /**
4390     * Joins the elements of the provided {@link List} into a single String
4391     * containing the provided list of elements.
4392     *
4393     * <p>No delimiter is added before or after the list.
4394     * Null objects or empty strings within the array are represented by
4395     * empty strings.</p>
4396     *
4397     * <pre>
4398     * StringUtils.join(null, *)               = null
4399     * StringUtils.join([], *)                 = ""
4400     * StringUtils.join([null], *)             = ""
4401     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"], ';')  = "a;b;c"
4402     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"], null) = "abc"
4403     * StringUtils.join([null, "", "a"], ';')  = ";;a"
4404     * </pre>
4405     *
4406     * @param list  the {@link List} of values to join together, may be null
4407     * @param separator  the separator character to use
4408     * @param startIndex the first index to start joining from.  It is
4409     * an error to pass in a start index past the end of the list
4410     * @param endIndex the index to stop joining from (exclusive). It is
4411     * an error to pass in an end index past the end of the list
4412     * @return the joined String, {@code null} if null list input
4413     * @since 3.8
4414     */
4415    public static String join(final List<?> list, final char separator, final int startIndex, final int endIndex) {
4416        if (list == null) {
4417            return null;
4418        }
4419        final int noOfItems = endIndex - startIndex;
4420        if (noOfItems <= 0) {
4421            return EMPTY;
4422        }
4423        final List<?> subList = list.subList(startIndex, endIndex);
4424        return join(subList.iterator(), separator);
4425    }
4426
4427    /**
4428     * Joins the elements of the provided {@link List} into a single String
4429     * containing the provided list of elements.
4430     *
4431     * <p>No delimiter is added before or after the list.
4432     * Null objects or empty strings within the array are represented by
4433     * empty strings.</p>
4434     *
4435     * <pre>
4436     * StringUtils.join(null, *)               = null
4437     * StringUtils.join([], *)                 = ""
4438     * StringUtils.join([null], *)             = ""
4439     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"], ';')  = "a;b;c"
4440     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"], null) = "abc"
4441     * StringUtils.join([null, "", "a"], ';')  = ";;a"
4442     * </pre>
4443     *
4444     * @param list  the {@link List} of values to join together, may be null
4445     * @param separator  the separator character to use
4446     * @param startIndex the first index to start joining from.  It is
4447     * an error to pass in a start index past the end of the list
4448     * @param endIndex the index to stop joining from (exclusive). It is
4449     * an error to pass in an end index past the end of the list
4450     * @return the joined String, {@code null} if null list input
4451     * @since 3.8
4452     */
4453    public static String join(final List<?> list, final String separator, final int startIndex, final int endIndex) {
4454        if (list == null) {
4455            return null;
4456        }
4457        final int noOfItems = endIndex - startIndex;
4458        if (noOfItems <= 0) {
4459            return EMPTY;
4460        }
4461        final List<?> subList = list.subList(startIndex, endIndex);
4462        return join(subList.iterator(), separator);
4463    }

4468     *
4469     * <p>

4471     * by empty strings.
4472     * </p>
4473     *
4474     * <pre>
4475     * StringUtils.join(null, *)               = null
4476     * StringUtils.join([], *)                 = ""
4477     * StringUtils.join([null], *)             = ""
4478     * StringUtils.join([1, 2, 3], ';')  = "1;2;3"
4479     * StringUtils.join([1, 2, 3], null) = "123"
4480     * </pre>
4481     *
4482     * @param array
4483     *            the array of values to join together, may be null
4484     * @param separator
4485     *            the separator character to use
4486     * @return the joined String, {@code null} if null array input
4487     * @since 3.2
4488     */
4489    public static String join(final long[] array, final char separator) {
4490        if (array == null) {
4491            return null;
4492        }
4493        return join(array, separator, 0, array.length);
4494    }

4496    /**
4497     * Joins the elements of the provided array into a single String containing the provided list of elements.
4498     *
4499     * <p>
4500     * No delimiter is added before or after the list. Null objects or empty strings within the array are represented
4501     * by empty strings.
4502     * </p>
4503     *
4504     * <pre>
4505     * StringUtils.join(null, *)               = null
4506     * StringUtils.join([], *)                 = ""
4507     * StringUtils.join([null], *)             = ""
4508     * StringUtils.join([1, 2, 3], ';')  = "1;2;3"
4509     * StringUtils.join([1, 2, 3], null) = "123"
4510     * </pre>
4511     *
4512     * @param array
4513     *            the array of values to join together, may be null
4514     * @param delimiter
4515     *            the separator character to use
4516     * @param startIndex
4517     *            the first index to start joining from. It is an error to pass in a start index past the end of the
4518     *            array
4519     * @param endIndex
4520     *            the index to stop joining from (exclusive). It is an error to pass in an end index past the end of
4521     *            the array
4522     * @return the joined String, {@code null} if null array input
4523     * @since 3.2
4524     */
4525    public static String join(final long[] array, final char delimiter, final int startIndex, final int endIndex) {
4526        if (array == null) {
4527            return null;
4528        }
4529        if (endIndex - startIndex <= 0) {
4530            return EMPTY;
4531        }
4532        final StringBuilder stringBuilder = new StringBuilder();
4533        for (int i = startIndex; i < endIndex; i++) {
4534            stringBuilder
4535                    .append(array[i])
4536                    .append(delimiter);
4537        }
4538        return stringBuilder.substring(0, stringBuilder.length() - 1);
4539    }

4565            return null;

4600    /**
4601     * Joins the elements of the provided array into a single String
4602     * containing the provided list of elements.
4603     *
4604     * <p>No delimiter is added before or after the list.
4605     * A {@code null} separator is the same as an empty String ("").
4606     * Null objects or empty strings within the array are represented by
4607     * empty strings.</p>
4608     *
4609     * <pre>
4610     * StringUtils.join(null, *)                = null
4611     * StringUtils.join([], *)                  = ""
4612     * StringUtils.join([null], *)              = ""
4613     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"], "--")  = "a--b--c"
4614     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"], null)  = "abc"
4615     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"], "")    = "abc"
4616     * StringUtils.join([null, "", "a"], ',')   = ",,a"
4617     * </pre>
4618     *
4619     * @param array  the array of values to join together, may be null
4620     * @param delimiter  the separator character to use, null treated as ""
4621     * @return the joined String, {@code null} if null array input
4622     */
4623    public static String join(final Object[] array, final String delimiter) {
4624        return array != null ? join(array, toStringOrEmpty(delimiter), 0, array.length) : null;
4625    }
4626
4627    /**
4628     * Joins the elements of the provided array into a single String
4629     * containing the provided list of elements.
4630     *
4631     * <p>No delimiter is added before or after the list.
4632     * A {@code null} separator is the same as an empty String ("").
4633     * Null objects or empty strings within the array are represented by
4634     * empty strings.</p>
4635     *
4636     * <pre>
4637     * StringUtils.join(null, *, *, *)                = null
4638     * StringUtils.join([], *, *, *)                  = ""
4639     * StringUtils.join([null], *, *, *)              = ""
4640     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"], "--", 0, 3)  = "a--b--c"
4641     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"], "--", 1, 3)  = "b--c"
4642     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"], "--", 2, 3)  = "c"
4643     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"], "--", 2, 2)  = ""
4644     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"], null, 0, 3)  = "abc"
4645     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"], "", 0, 3)    = "abc"
4646     * StringUtils.join([null, "", "a"], ',', 0, 3)   = ",,a"
4647     * </pre>
4648     *
4649     * @param array  the array of values to join together, may be null
4650     * @param delimiter  the separator character to use, null treated as ""
4651     * @param startIndex the first index to start joining from.
4652     * @param endIndex the index to stop joining from (exclusive).
4653     * @return the joined String, {@code null} if null array input; or the empty string
4654     * if {@code endIndex - startIndex <= 0}. The number of joined entries is given by
4655     * {@code endIndex - startIndex}
4656     * @throws ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException ife<br>
4657     * {@code startIndex < 0} or <br>
4658     * {@code startIndex >= array.length()} or <br>
4659     * {@code endIndex < 0} or <br>
4660     * {@code endIndex > array.length()}
4661     */
4662    public static String join(final Object[] array, final String delimiter, final int startIndex, final int endIndex) {
4663        return array != null ? Streams.of(array).skip(startIndex).limit(Math.max(0, endIndex - startIndex))
4664            .collect(LangCollectors.joining(delimiter, EMPTY, EMPTY, StringUtils::toStringOrEmpty)) : null;
4665    }

4708     * StringUtils.join([null], *)             = ""

4722     *            the array

4742    /**
4743     * Joins the elements of the provided array into a single String
4744     * containing the provided list of elements.

4748     * empty strings.</p>

4751     * StringUtils.join(null)            = null
4752     * StringUtils.join([])              = ""
4753     * StringUtils.join([null])          = ""
4754     * StringUtils.join(["a", "b", "c"]) = "abc"
4755     * StringUtils.join([null, "", "a"]) = "a"
4756     * </pre>
4757     *
4758     * @param <T> the specific type of values to join together
4759     * @param elements  the values to join together, may be null
4760     * @return the joined String, {@code null} if null array input
4761     * @since 2.0
4762     * @since 3.0 Changed signature to use varargs

4764    @SafeVarargs
4765    public static <T> String join(final T... elements) {

4769    /**
4770     * Joins the elements of the provided varargs into a
4771     * single String containing the provided elements.
4772     *
4773     * <p>No delimiter is added before or after the list.
4774     * {@code null} elements and separator are treated as empty Strings ("").</p>
4775     *
4776     * <pre>
4777     * StringUtils.joinWith(",", {"a", "b"})        = "a,b"
4778     * StringUtils.joinWith(",", {"a", "b",""})     = "a,b,"
4779     * StringUtils.joinWith(",", {"a", null, "b"})  = "a,,b"
4780     * StringUtils.joinWith(null, {"a", "b"})       = "ab"
4781     * </pre>
4782     *

4784     * @param array the varargs providing the values to join together. {@code null} elements are treated as ""
4785     * @return the joined String.
4786     * @throws IllegalArgumentException if a null varargs is provided
4787     * @since 3.5
4788     */
4789    public static String joinWith(final String delimiter, final Object... array) {
4790        if (array == null) {
4791            throw new IllegalArgumentException("Object varargs must not be null");
4792        }
4793        return join(array, delimiter);
4794    }

4796    /**
4797     * Finds the last index within a CharSequence, handling {@code null}.
4798     * This method uses {@link String#lastIndexOf(String)} if possible.
4799     *
4800     * <p>A {@code null} CharSequence will return {@code -1}.</p>
4801     *
4802     * <pre>
4803     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf(null, *)          = -1
4804     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf(*, null)          = -1
4805     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("", "")           = 0
4806     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "a")  = 7
4807     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "b")  = 5
4808     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "ab") = 4
4809     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "")   = 8
4810     * </pre>
4811     *
4812     * @param seq  the CharSequence to check, may be null
4813     * @param searchSeq  the CharSequence to find, may be null
4814     * @return the last index of the search String,
4815     *  -1 if no match or {@code null} string input
4816     * @since 2.0
4817     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from lastIndexOf(String, String) to lastIndexOf(CharSequence, CharSequence)
4818     */
4819    public static int lastIndexOf(final CharSequence seq, final CharSequence searchSeq) {
4820        if (seq == null) {
4821            return INDEX_NOT_FOUND;
4822        }
4823        return CharSequenceUtils.lastIndexOf(seq, searchSeq, seq.length());
4824    }
4825
4826    /**
4827     * Finds the last index within a CharSequence, handling {@code null}.
4828     * This method uses {@link String#lastIndexOf(String, int)} if possible.
4829     *
4830     * <p>A {@code null} CharSequence will return {@code -1}.
4831     * A negative start position returns {@code -1}.
4832     * An empty ("") search CharSequence always matches unless the start position is negative.
4833     * A start position greater than the string length searches the whole string.
4834     * The search starts at the startPos and works backwards; matches starting after the start
4835     * position are ignored.
4836     * </p>
4837     *
4838     * <pre>
4839     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf(null, *, *)          = -1
4840     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf(*, null, *)          = -1
4841     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "a", 8)  = 7
4842     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "b", 8)  = 5
4843     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "ab", 8) = 4
4844     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "b", 9)  = 5
4845     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "b", -1) = -1
4846     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "a", 0)  = 0
4847     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "b", 0)  = -1
4848     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "b", 1)  = -1
4849     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "b", 2)  = 2
4850     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", "ba", 2)  = 2
4851     * </pre>
4852     *
4853     * @param seq  the CharSequence to check, may be null
4854     * @param searchSeq  the CharSequence to find, may be null
4855     * @param startPos  the start position, negative treated as zero
4856     * @return the last index of the search CharSequence (always &le; startPos),
4857     *  -1 if no match or {@code null} string input
4858     * @since 2.0
4859     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from lastIndexOf(String, String, int) to lastIndexOf(CharSequence, CharSequence, int)
4860     */
4861    public static int lastIndexOf(final CharSequence seq, final CharSequence searchSeq, final int startPos) {
4862        return CharSequenceUtils.lastIndexOf(seq, searchSeq, startPos);
4863    }
4864
4865    /**
4866     * Returns the index within {@code seq} of the last occurrence of
4867     * the specified character. For values of {@code searchChar} in the
4868     * range from 0 to 0xFFFF (inclusive), the index (in Unicode code
4869     * units) returned is the largest value <i>k</i> such that:
4870     * <blockquote><pre>
4871     * this.charAt(<i>k</i>) == searchChar
4872     * </pre></blockquote>
4873     * is true. For other values of {@code searchChar}, it is the
4874     * largest value <i>k</i> such that:
4875     * <blockquote><pre>
4876     * this.codePointAt(<i>k</i>) == searchChar
4877     * </pre></blockquote>
4878     * is true.  In either case, if no such character occurs in this
4879     * string, then {@code -1} is returned. Furthermore, a {@code null} or empty ("")
4880     * {@link CharSequence} will return {@code -1}. The
4881     * {@code seq} {@link CharSequence} object is searched backwards
4882     * starting at the last character.
4883     *
4884     * <pre>
4885     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf(null, *)         = -1
4886     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("", *)           = -1
4887     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", 'a') = 7
4888     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", 'b') = 5
4889     * </pre>
4890     *
4891     * @param seq  the {@link CharSequence} to check, may be null
4892     * @param searchChar  the character to find
4893     * @return the last index of the search character,
4894     *  -1 if no match or {@code null} string input
4895     * @since 2.0
4896     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from lastIndexOf(String, int) to lastIndexOf(CharSequence, int)
4897     * @since 3.6 Updated {@link CharSequenceUtils} call to behave more like {@link String}
4898     */
4899    public static int lastIndexOf(final CharSequence seq, final int searchChar) {
4900        if (isEmpty(seq)) {
4901            return INDEX_NOT_FOUND;
4902        }
4903        return CharSequenceUtils.lastIndexOf(seq, searchChar, seq.length());
4904    }
4905
4906    /**
4907     * Returns the index within {@code seq} of the last occurrence of
4908     * the specified character, searching backward starting at the
4909     * specified index. For values of {@code searchChar} in the range
4910     * from 0 to 0xFFFF (inclusive), the index returned is the largest
4911     * value <i>k</i> such that:
4912     * <blockquote><pre>
4913     * (this.charAt(<i>k</i>) == searchChar) &amp;&amp; (<i>k</i> &lt;= startPos)
4914     * </pre></blockquote>
4915     * is true. For other values of {@code searchChar}, it is the
4916     * largest value <i>k</i> such that:
4917     * <blockquote><pre>
4918     * (this.codePointAt(<i>k</i>) == searchChar) &amp;&amp; (<i>k</i> &lt;= startPos)
4919     * </pre></blockquote>
4920     * is true. In either case, if no such character occurs in {@code seq}
4921     * at or before position {@code startPos}, then
4922     * {@code -1} is returned. Furthermore, a {@code null} or empty ("")
4923     * {@link CharSequence} will return {@code -1}. A start position greater
4924     * than the string length searches the whole string.
4925     * The search starts at the {@code startPos} and works backwards;
4926     * matches starting after the start position are ignored.
4927     *
4928     * <p>All indices are specified in {@code char} values
4929     * (Unicode code units).
4930     *
4931     * <pre>
4932     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf(null, *, *)          = -1
4933     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("", *,  *)           = -1
4934     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", 'b', 8)  = 5
4935     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", 'b', 4)  = 2
4936     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", 'b', 0)  = -1
4937     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", 'b', 9)  = 5
4938     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", 'b', -1) = -1
4939     * StringUtils.lastIndexOf("aabaabaa", 'a', 0)  = 0
4940     * </pre>
4941     *
4942     * @param seq  the CharSequence to check, may be null
4943     * @param searchChar  the character to find
4944     * @param startPos  the start position
4945     * @return the last index of the search character (always &le; startPos),
4946     *  -1 if no match or {@code null} string input
4947     * @since 2.0
4948     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from lastIndexOf(String, int, int) to lastIndexOf(CharSequence, int, int)
4949     */
4950    public static int lastIndexOf(final CharSequence seq, final int searchChar, final int startPos) {
4951        if (isEmpty(seq)) {
4952            return INDEX_NOT_FOUND;
4953        }
4954        return CharSequenceUtils.lastIndexOf(seq, searchChar, startPos);
4955    }
4956
4957    /**
4958     * Find the latest index of any substring in a set of potential substrings.
4959     *
4960     * <p>A {@code null} CharSequence will return {@code -1}.
4961     * A {@code null} search array will return {@code -1}.
4962     * A {@code null} or zero length search array entry will be ignored,
4963     * but a search array containing "" will return the length of {@code str}
4964     * if {@code str} is not null. This method uses {@link String#indexOf(String)} if possible</p>
4965     *
4966     * <pre>
4967     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfAny(null, *)                    = -1
4968     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfAny(*, null)                    = -1
4969     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfAny(*, [])                      = -1
4970     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfAny(*, [null])                  = -1
4971     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfAny("zzabyycdxx", ["ab", "cd"]) = 6
4972     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfAny("zzabyycdxx", ["cd", "ab"]) = 6
4973     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfAny("zzabyycdxx", ["mn", "op"]) = -1
4974     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfAny("zzabyycdxx", ["mn", "op"]) = -1
4975     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfAny("zzabyycdxx", ["mn", ""])   = 10
4976     * </pre>
4977     *
4978     * @param str  the CharSequence to check, may be null
4979     * @param searchStrs  the CharSequences to search for, may be null
4980     * @return the last index of any of the CharSequences, -1 if no match
4981     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from lastIndexOfAny(String, String[]) to lastIndexOfAny(CharSequence, CharSequence)
4982     */
4983    public static int lastIndexOfAny(final CharSequence str, final CharSequence... searchStrs) {
4984        if (str == null || searchStrs == null) {
4985            return INDEX_NOT_FOUND;
4986        }
4987        int ret = INDEX_NOT_FOUND;
4988        int tmp;
4989        for (final CharSequence search : searchStrs) {
4990            if (search == null) {
4991                continue;
4992            }
4993            tmp = CharSequenceUtils.lastIndexOf(str, search, str.length());
4994            if (tmp > ret) {
4995                ret = tmp;
4996            }
4997        }
4998        return ret;
4999    }

5001    /**
5002     * Case in-sensitive find of the last index within a CharSequence.
5003     *
5004     * <p>A {@code null} CharSequence will return {@code -1}.
5005     * A negative start position returns {@code -1}.
5006     * An empty ("") search CharSequence always matches unless the start position is negative.
5007     * A start position greater than the string length searches the whole string.</p>
5008     *
5009     * <pre>
5010     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase(null, *)          = -1
5011     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase(*, null)          = -1
5012     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase("aabaabaa", "A")  = 7
5013     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase("aabaabaa", "B")  = 5
5014     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase("aabaabaa", "AB") = 4
5015     * </pre>
5016     *
5017     * @param str  the CharSequence to check, may be null
5018     * @param searchStr  the CharSequence to find, may be null
5019     * @return the first index of the search CharSequence,
5020     *  -1 if no match or {@code null} string input
5021     * @since 2.5
5022     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from lastIndexOfIgnoreCase(String, String) to lastIndexOfIgnoreCase(CharSequence, CharSequence)
5023     */
5024    public static int lastIndexOfIgnoreCase(final CharSequence str, final CharSequence searchStr) {
5025        if (str == null || searchStr == null) {
5026            return INDEX_NOT_FOUND;
5027        }
5028        return lastIndexOfIgnoreCase(str, searchStr, str.length());
5029    }
5030
5031    /**
5032     * Case in-sensitive find of the last index within a CharSequence
5033     * from the specified position.
5034     *
5035     * <p>A {@code null} CharSequence will return {@code -1}.
5036     * A negative start position returns {@code -1}.
5037     * An empty ("") search CharSequence always matches unless the start position is negative.
5038     * A start position greater than the string length searches the whole string.
5039     * The search starts at the startPos and works backwards; matches starting after the start
5040     * position are ignored.
5041     * </p>
5042     *
5043     * <pre>
5044     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase(null, *, *)          = -1
5045     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase(*, null, *)          = -1
5046     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase("aabaabaa", "A", 8)  = 7
5047     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase("aabaabaa", "B", 8)  = 5
5048     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase("aabaabaa", "AB", 8) = 4
5049     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase("aabaabaa", "B", 9)  = 5
5050     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase("aabaabaa", "B", -1) = -1
5051     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase("aabaabaa", "A", 0)  = 0
5052     * StringUtils.lastIndexOfIgnoreCase("aabaabaa", "B", 0)  = -1
5053     * </pre>
5054     *
5055     * @param str  the CharSequence to check, may be null
5056     * @param searchStr  the CharSequence to find, may be null
5057     * @param startPos  the start position
5058     * @return the last index of the search CharSequence (always &le; startPos),
5059     *  -1 if no match or {@code null} input
5060     * @since 2.5
5061     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from lastIndexOfIgnoreCase(String, String, int) to lastIndexOfIgnoreCase(CharSequence, CharSequence, int)
5062     */
5063    public static int lastIndexOfIgnoreCase(final CharSequence str, final CharSequence searchStr, int startPos) {
5064        if (str == null || searchStr == null) {
5065            return INDEX_NOT_FOUND;
5066        }
5067        final int searchStrLength = searchStr.length();
5068        final int strLength = str.length();
5069        if (startPos > strLength - searchStrLength) {
5070            startPos = strLength - searchStrLength;
5071        }
5072        if (startPos < 0) {
5073            return INDEX_NOT_FOUND;
5074        }
5075        if (searchStrLength == 0) {
5076            return startPos;
5077        }
5078
5079        for (int i = startPos; i >= 0; i--) {
5080            if (CharSequenceUtils.regionMatches(str, true, i, searchStr, 0, searchStrLength)) {
5081                return i;
5082            }
5083        }
5084        return INDEX_NOT_FOUND;
5085    }

5087    /**
5088     * Finds the n-th last index within a String, handling {@code null}.
5089     * This method uses {@link String#lastIndexOf(String)}.
5090     *
5091     * <p>A {@code null} String will return {@code -1}.</p>
5092     *
5093     * <pre>
5094     * StringUtils.lastOrdinalIndexOf(null, *, *)          = -1
5095     * StringUtils.lastOrdinalIndexOf(*, null, *)          = -1
5096     * StringUtils.lastOrdinalIndexOf("", "", *)           = 0
5097     * StringUtils.lastOrdinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "a", 1)  = 7
5098     * StringUtils.lastOrdinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "a", 2)  = 6
5099     * StringUtils.lastOrdinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "b", 1)  = 5
5100     * StringUtils.lastOrdinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "b", 2)  = 2
5101     * StringUtils.lastOrdinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "ab", 1) = 4
5102     * StringUtils.lastOrdinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "ab", 2) = 1
5103     * StringUtils.lastOrdinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "", 1)   = 8
5104     * StringUtils.lastOrdinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "", 2)   = 8
5105     * </pre>
5106     *
5107     * <p>Note that 'tail(CharSequence str, int n)' may be implemented as: </p>
5108     *
5109     * <pre>
5110     *   str.substring(lastOrdinalIndexOf(str, "\n", n) + 1)
5111     * </pre>
5112     *
5113     * @param str  the CharSequence to check, may be null
5114     * @param searchStr  the CharSequence to find, may be null
5115     * @param ordinal  the n-th last {@code searchStr} to find
5116     * @return the n-th last index of the search CharSequence,
5117     *  {@code -1} ({@code INDEX_NOT_FOUND}) if no match or {@code null} string input
5118     * @since 2.5
5119     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from lastOrdinalIndexOf(String, String, int) to lastOrdinalIndexOf(CharSequence, CharSequence, int)
5120     */
5121    public static int lastOrdinalIndexOf(final CharSequence str, final CharSequence searchStr, final int ordinal) {
5122        return ordinalIndexOf(str, searchStr, ordinal, true);
5123    }

5125    /**
5126     * Gets the leftmost {@code len} characters of a String.
5127     *
5128     * <p>If {@code len} characters are not available, or the
5129     * String is {@code null}, the String will be returned without
5130     * an exception. An empty String is returned if len is negative.</p>
5131     *
5132     * <pre>
5133     * StringUtils.left(null, *)    = null
5134     * StringUtils.left(*, -ve)     = ""
5135     * StringUtils.left("", *)      = ""
5136     * StringUtils.left("abc", 0)   = ""
5137     * StringUtils.left("abc", 2)   = "ab"
5138     * StringUtils.left("abc", 4)   = "abc"
5139     * </pre>
5140     *
5141     * @param str  the String to get the leftmost characters from, may be null
5142     * @param len  the length of the required String
5143     * @return the leftmost characters, {@code null} if null String input
5144     */
5145    public static String left(final String str, final int len) {
5146        if (str == null) {
5147            return null;
5148        }
5149        if (len < 0) {
5150            return EMPTY;
5151        }
5152        if (str.length() <= len) {
5153            return str;
5154        }
5155        return str.substring(0, len);
5156    }

5158    /**
5159     * Left pad a String with spaces (' ').
5160     *
5161     * <p>The String is padded to the size of {@code size}.</p>
5162     *
5163     * <pre>
5164     * StringUtils.leftPad(null, *)   = null
5165     * StringUtils.leftPad("", 3)     = "   "
5166     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", 3)  = "bat"
5167     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", 5)  = "  bat"
5168     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", 1)  = "bat"
5169     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", -1) = "bat"
5170     * </pre>
5171     *
5172     * @param str  the String to pad out, may be null
5173     * @param size  the size to pad to
5174     * @return left padded String or original String if no padding is necessary,
5175     *  {@code null} if null String input
5176     */
5177    public static String leftPad(final String str, final int size) {
5178        return leftPad(str, size, ' ');
5179    }

5181    /**
5182     * Left pad a String with a specified character.
5183     *
5184     * <p>Pad to a size of {@code size}.</p>
5185     *
5186     * <pre>
5187     * StringUtils.leftPad(null, *, *)     = null
5188     * StringUtils.leftPad("", 3, 'z')     = "zzz"
5189     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", 3, 'z')  = "bat"
5190     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", 5, 'z')  = "zzbat"
5191     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", 1, 'z')  = "bat"
5192     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", -1, 'z') = "bat"
5193     * </pre>
5194     *
5195     * @param str  the String to pad out, may be null
5196     * @param size  the size to pad to
5197     * @param padChar  the character to pad with
5198     * @return left padded String or original String if no padding is necessary,
5199     *  {@code null} if null String input
5200     * @since 2.0
5201     */
5202    public static String leftPad(final String str, final int size, final char padChar) {
5203        if (str == null) {
5204            return null;
5205        }
5206        final int pads = size - str.length();
5207        if (pads <= 0) {
5208            return str; // returns original String when possible
5209        }
5210        if (pads > PAD_LIMIT) {
5211            return leftPad(str, size, String.valueOf(padChar));
5212        }
5213        return repeat(padChar, pads).concat(str);
5214    }
5215
5216    /**
5217     * Left pad a String with a specified String.
5218     *
5219     * <p>Pad to a size of {@code size}.</p>
5220     *
5221     * <pre>
5222     * StringUtils.leftPad(null, *, *)      = null
5223     * StringUtils.leftPad("", 3, "z")      = "zzz"
5224     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", 3, "yz")  = "bat"
5225     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", 5, "yz")  = "yzbat"
5226     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", 8, "yz")  = "yzyzybat"
5227     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", 1, "yz")  = "bat"
5228     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", -1, "yz") = "bat"
5229     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", 5, null)  = "  bat"
5230     * StringUtils.leftPad("bat", 5, "")    = "  bat"
5231     * </pre>
5232     *
5233     * @param str  the String to pad out, may be null
5234     * @param size  the size to pad to
5235     * @param padStr  the String to pad with, null or empty treated as single space
5236     * @return left padded String or original String if no padding is necessary,
5237     *  {@code null} if null String input
5238     */
5239    public static String leftPad(final String str, final int size, String padStr) {
5240        if (str == null) {
5241            return null;
5242        }
5243        if (isEmpty(padStr)) {
5244            padStr = SPACE;
5245        }
5246        final int padLen = padStr.length();
5247        final int strLen = str.length();
5248        final int pads = size - strLen;
5249        if (pads <= 0) {
5250            return str; // returns original String when possible
5251        }
5252        if (padLen == 1 && pads <= PAD_LIMIT) {
5253            return leftPad(str, size, padStr.charAt(0));
5254        }
5255
5256        if (pads == padLen) {
5257            return padStr.concat(str);
5258        }
5259        if (pads < padLen) {
5260            return padStr.substring(0, pads).concat(str);
5261        }
5262        final char[] padding = new char[pads];
5263        final char[] padChars = padStr.toCharArray();
5264        for (int i = 0; i < pads; i++) {
5265            padding[i] = padChars[i % padLen];
5266        }
5267        return new String(padding).concat(str);
5268    }

5272     * {@code null}.
5273     *
5274     * @param cs
5275     *            a CharSequence or {@code null}
5276     * @return CharSequence length or {@code 0} if the CharSequence is
5277     *         {@code null}.
5278     * @since 2.4
5279     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from length(String) to length(CharSequence)
5280     */
5281    public static int length(final CharSequence cs) {
5282        return cs == null ? 0 : cs.length();
5283    }

5285    /**
5286     * Converts a String to lower case as per {@link String#toLowerCase()}.

5291     * StringUtils.lowerCase(null)  = null
5292     * StringUtils.lowerCase("")    = ""
5293     * StringUtils.lowerCase("aBc") = "abc"
5294     * </pre>
5295     *
5296     * <p><strong>Note:</strong> As described in the documentation for {@link String#toLowerCase()},
5297     * the result of this method is affected by the current locale.
5298     * For platform-independent case transformations, the method {@link #lowerCase(String, Locale)}
5299     * should be used with a specific locale (e.g. {@link Locale#ENGLISH}).</p>
5300     *
5301     * @param str  the String to lower case, may be null
5302     * @return the lower cased String, {@code null} if null String input
5303     */
5304    public static String lowerCase(final String str) {

5306            return null;

5311    /**
5312     * Converts a String to lower case as per {@link String#toLowerCase(Locale)}.
5313     *
5314     * <p>A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.</p>
5315     *
5316     * <pre>
5317     * StringUtils.lowerCase(null, Locale.ENGLISH)  = null
5318     * StringUtils.lowerCase("", Locale.ENGLISH)    = ""
5319     * StringUtils.lowerCase("aBc", Locale.ENGLISH) = "abc"
5320     * </pre>
5321     *
5322     * @param str  the String to lower case, may be null
5323     * @param locale  the locale that defines the case transformation rules, must not be null
5324     * @return the lower cased String, {@code null} if null String input
5325     * @since 2.5
5326     */
5327    public static String lowerCase(final String str, final Locale locale) {
5328        if (str == null) {
5329            return null;

5331        return str.toLowerCase(LocaleUtils.toLocale(locale));

5333
5334    private static int[] matches(final CharSequence first, final CharSequence second) {
5335        final CharSequence max;
5336        final CharSequence min;
5337        if (first.length() > second.length()) {
5338            max = first;
5339            min = second;
5340        } else {
5341            max = second;
5342            min = first;
5343        }
5344        final int range = Math.max(max.length() / 2 - 1, 0);
5345        final int[] matchIndexes = new int[min.length()];
5346        Arrays.fill(matchIndexes, -1);
5347        final boolean[] matchFlags = new boolean[max.length()];
5348        int matches = 0;
5349        for (int mi = 0; mi < min.length(); mi++) {
5350            final char c1 = min.charAt(mi);
5351            for (int xi = Math.max(mi - range, 0), xn = Math.min(mi + range + 1, max.length()); xi < xn; xi++) {
5352                if (!matchFlags[xi] && c1 == max.charAt(xi)) {
5353                    matchIndexes[mi] = xi;
5354                    matchFlags[xi] = true;
5355                    matches++;
5356                    break;
5357                }
5358            }
5359        }
5360        final char[] ms1 = new char[matches];
5361        final char[] ms2 = new char[matches];
5362        for (int i = 0, si = 0; i < min.length(); i++) {
5363            if (matchIndexes[i] != -1) {
5364                ms1[si] = min.charAt(i);
5365                si++;
5366            }
5367        }
5368        for (int i = 0, si = 0; i < max.length(); i++) {
5369            if (matchFlags[i]) {
5370                ms2[si] = max.charAt(i);
5371                si++;
5372            }
5373        }
5374        int transpositions = 0;
5375        for (int mi = 0; mi < ms1.length; mi++) {
5376            if (ms1[mi] != ms2[mi]) {
5377                transpositions++;
5378            }
5379        }
5380        int prefix = 0;
5381        for (int mi = 0; mi < min.length(); mi++) {
5382            if (first.charAt(mi) != second.charAt(mi)) {
5383                break;
5384            }
5385            prefix++;
5386        }
5387        return new int[] { matches, transpositions / 2, prefix, max.length() };
5388    }
5389
5390    /**
5391     * Gets {@code len} characters from the middle of a String.
5392     *
5393     * <p>If {@code len} characters are not available, the remainder
5394     * of the String will be returned without an exception. If the
5395     * String is {@code null}, {@code null} will be returned.
5396     * An empty String is returned if len is negative or exceeds the
5397     * length of {@code str}.</p>
5398     *
5399     * <pre>
5400     * StringUtils.mid(null, *, *)    = null
5401     * StringUtils.mid(*, *, -ve)     = ""
5402     * StringUtils.mid("", 0, *)      = ""
5403     * StringUtils.mid("abc", 0, 2)   = "ab"
5404     * StringUtils.mid("abc", 0, 4)   = "abc"
5405     * StringUtils.mid("abc", 2, 4)   = "c"
5406     * StringUtils.mid("abc", 4, 2)   = ""
5407     * StringUtils.mid("abc", -2, 2)  = "ab"
5408     * </pre>
5409     *
5410     * @param str  the String to get the characters from, may be null
5411     * @param pos  the position to start from, negative treated as zero
5412     * @param len  the length of the required String
5413     * @return the middle characters, {@code null} if null String input
5414     */
5415    public static String mid(final String str, int pos, final int len) {
5416        if (str == null) {
5417            return null;
5418        }
5419        if (len < 0 || pos > str.length()) {
5420            return EMPTY;
5421        }
5422        if (pos < 0) {
5423            pos = 0;
5424        }
5425        if (str.length() <= pos + len) {
5426            return str.substring(pos);
5427        }
5428        return str.substring(pos, pos + len);
5429    }
5430
5431    /**
5432     * Similar to <a
5433     * href="https://www.w3.org/TR/xpath/#function-normalize-space">https://www.w3.org/TR/xpath/#function-normalize
5434     * -space</a>
5435     *
5436     * <p>
5437     * The function returns the argument string with whitespace normalized by using
5438     * {@code {@link #trim(String)}} to remove leading and trailing whitespace
5439     * and then replacing sequences of whitespace characters by a single space.
5440     * </p>
5441     * In XML Whitespace characters are the same as those allowed by the <a
5442     * href="https://www.w3.org/TR/REC-xml/#NT-S">S</a> production, which is S ::= (#x20 | #x9 | #xD | #xA)+
5443     * <p>
5444     * Java's regexp pattern \s defines whitespace as [ \t\n\x0B\f\r]
5445     *
5446     * <p>For reference:</p>
5447     * <ul>
5448     * <li>\x0B = vertical tab</li>
5449     * <li>\f = #xC = form feed</li>
5450     * <li>#x20 = space</li>
5451     * <li>#x9 = \t</li>
5452     * <li>#xA = \n</li>
5453     * <li>#xD = \r</li>
5454     * </ul>
5455     *
5456     * <p>
5457     * The difference is that Java's whitespace includes vertical tab and form feed, which this functional will also
5458     * normalize. Additionally {@code {@link #trim(String)}} removes control characters (char &lt;= 32) from both
5459     * ends of this String.
5460     * </p>
5461     *
5462     * @see Pattern
5463     * @see #trim(String)
5464     * @see <a
5465     *      href="https://www.w3.org/TR/xpath/#function-normalize-space">https://www.w3.org/TR/xpath/#function-normalize-space</a>
5466     * @param str the source String to normalize whitespaces from, may be null
5467     * @return the modified string with whitespace normalized, {@code null} if null String input
5468     *
5469     * @since 3.0
5470     */
5471    public static String normalizeSpace(final String str) {
5472        // LANG-1020: Improved performance significantly by normalizing manually instead of using regex
5473        // See https://github.com/librucha/commons-lang-normalizespaces-benchmark for performance test
5474        if (isEmpty(str)) {
5475            return str;
5476        }
5477        final int size = str.length();
5478        final char[] newChars = new char[size];
5479        int count = 0;
5480        int whitespacesCount = 0;
5481        boolean startWhitespaces = true;
5482        for (int i = 0; i < size; i++) {
5483            final char actualChar = str.charAt(i);
5484            final boolean isWhitespace = Character.isWhitespace(actualChar);
5485            if (isWhitespace) {
5486                if (whitespacesCount == 0 && !startWhitespaces) {
5487                    newChars[count++] = SPACE.charAt(0);
5488                }
5489                whitespacesCount++;
5490            } else {
5491                startWhitespaces = false;
5492                newChars[count++] = actualChar == 160 ? 32 : actualChar;
5493                whitespacesCount = 0;
5494            }
5495        }
5496        if (startWhitespaces) {
5497            return EMPTY;
5498        }
5499        return new String(newChars, 0, count - (whitespacesCount > 0 ? 1 : 0)).trim();
5500    }
5501
5502    /**
5503     * Finds the n-th index within a CharSequence, handling {@code null}.
5504     * This method uses {@link String#indexOf(String)} if possible.
5505     * <p><b>Note:</b> The code starts looking for a match at the start of the target,
5506     * incrementing the starting index by one after each successful match
5507     * (unless {@code searchStr} is an empty string in which case the position
5508     * is never incremented and {@code 0} is returned immediately).
5509     * This means that matches may overlap.</p>
5510     * <p>A {@code null} CharSequence will return {@code -1}.</p>
5511     *
5512     * <pre>
5513     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf(null, *, *)          = -1
5514     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf(*, null, *)          = -1
5515     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("", "", *)           = 0
5516     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "a", 1)  = 0
5517     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "a", 2)  = 1
5518     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "b", 1)  = 2
5519     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "b", 2)  = 5
5520     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "ab", 1) = 1
5521     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "ab", 2) = 4
5522     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "", 1)   = 0
5523     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("aabaabaa", "", 2)   = 0
5524     * </pre>
5525     *
5526     * <p>Matches may overlap:</p>
5527     * <pre>
5528     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("ababab", "aba", 1)   = 0
5529     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("ababab", "aba", 2)   = 2
5530     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("ababab", "aba", 3)   = -1
5531     *
5532     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("abababab", "abab", 1) = 0
5533     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("abababab", "abab", 2) = 2
5534     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("abababab", "abab", 3) = 4
5535     * StringUtils.ordinalIndexOf("abababab", "abab", 4) = -1
5536     * </pre>
5537     *
5538     * <p>Note that 'head(CharSequence str, int n)' may be implemented as: </p>
5539     *
5540     * <pre>
5541     *   str.substring(0, lastOrdinalIndexOf(str, "\n", n))
5542     * </pre>
5543     *
5544     * @param str  the CharSequence to check, may be null
5545     * @param searchStr  the CharSequence to find, may be null
5546     * @param ordinal  the n-th {@code searchStr} to find
5547     * @return the n-th index of the search CharSequence,
5548     *  {@code -1} ({@code INDEX_NOT_FOUND}) if no match or {@code null} string input
5549     * @since 2.1
5550     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from ordinalIndexOf(String, String, int) to ordinalIndexOf(CharSequence, CharSequence, int)
5551     */
5552    public static int ordinalIndexOf(final CharSequence str, final CharSequence searchStr, final int ordinal) {
5553        return ordinalIndexOf(str, searchStr, ordinal, false);
5554    }
5555
5556    /**
5557     * Finds the n-th index within a String, handling {@code null}.
5558     * This method uses {@link String#indexOf(String)} if possible.
5559     * <p>Note that matches may overlap<p>
5560     *
5561     * <p>A {@code null} CharSequence will return {@code -1}.</p>
5562     *
5563     * @param str  the CharSequence to check, may be null
5564     * @param searchStr  the CharSequence to find, may be null
5565     * @param ordinal  the n-th {@code searchStr} to find, overlapping matches are allowed.
5566     * @param lastIndex true if lastOrdinalIndexOf() otherwise false if ordinalIndexOf()
5567     * @return the n-th index of the search CharSequence,
5568     *  {@code -1} ({@code INDEX_NOT_FOUND}) if no match or {@code null} string input
5569     */
5570    // Shared code between ordinalIndexOf(String, String, int) and lastOrdinalIndexOf(String, String, int)
5571    private static int ordinalIndexOf(final CharSequence str, final CharSequence searchStr, final int ordinal, final boolean lastIndex) {
5572        if (str == null || searchStr == null || ordinal <= 0) {
5573            return INDEX_NOT_FOUND;
5574        }
5575        if (searchStr.length() == 0) {
5576            return lastIndex ? str.length() : 0;
5577        }
5578        int found = 0;
5579        // set the initial index beyond the end of the string
5580        // this is to allow for the initial index decrement/increment
5581        int index = lastIndex ? str.length() : INDEX_NOT_FOUND;
5582        do {
5583            if (lastIndex) {
5584                index = CharSequenceUtils.lastIndexOf(str, searchStr, index - 1); // step backwards through string
5585            } else {
5586                index = CharSequenceUtils.indexOf(str, searchStr, index + 1); // step forwards through string
5587            }
5588            if (index < 0) {
5589                return index;
5590            }
5591            found++;
5592        } while (found < ordinal);
5593        return index;
5594    }
5595
5596    /**
5597     * Overlays part of a String with another String.
5598     *
5599     * <p>A {@code null} string input returns {@code null}.
5600     * A negative index is treated as zero.
5601     * An index greater than the string length is treated as the string length.
5602     * The start index is always the smaller of the two indices.</p>
5603     *
5604     * <pre>
5605     * StringUtils.overlay(null, *, *, *)            = null
5606     * StringUtils.overlay("", "abc", 0, 0)          = "abc"
5607     * StringUtils.overlay("abcdef", null, 2, 4)     = "abef"
5608     * StringUtils.overlay("abcdef", "", 2, 4)       = "abef"
5609     * StringUtils.overlay("abcdef", "", 4, 2)       = "abef"
5610     * StringUtils.overlay("abcdef", "zzzz", 2, 4)   = "abzzzzef"
5611     * StringUtils.overlay("abcdef", "zzzz", 4, 2)   = "abzzzzef"
5612     * StringUtils.overlay("abcdef", "zzzz", -1, 4)  = "zzzzef"
5613     * StringUtils.overlay("abcdef", "zzzz", 2, 8)   = "abzzzz"
5614     * StringUtils.overlay("abcdef", "zzzz", -2, -3) = "zzzzabcdef"
5615     * StringUtils.overlay("abcdef", "zzzz", 8, 10)  = "abcdefzzzz"
5616     * </pre>
5617     *
5618     * @param str  the String to do overlaying in, may be null
5619     * @param overlay  the String to overlay, may be null
5620     * @param start  the position to start overlaying at
5621     * @param end  the position to stop overlaying before
5622     * @return overlayed String, {@code null} if null String input
5623     * @since 2.0
5624     */
5625    public static String overlay(final String str, String overlay, int start, int end) {
5626        if (str == null) {
5627            return null;
5628        }
5629        if (overlay == null) {
5630            overlay = EMPTY;
5631        }
5632        final int len = str.length();
5633        if (start < 0) {
5634            start = 0;
5635        }
5636        if (start > len) {
5637            start = len;
5638        }
5639        if (end < 0) {
5640            end = 0;
5641        }
5642        if (end > len) {
5643            end = len;
5644        }
5645        if (start > end) {
5646            final int temp = start;
5647            start = end;
5648            end = temp;
5649        }
5650        return str.substring(0, start) +
5651            overlay +
5652            str.substring(end);
5653    }
5654
5655    /**
5656     * Prepends the prefix to the start of the string if the string does not
5657     * already start with any of the prefixes.
5658     *
5659     * @param str The string.
5660     * @param prefix The prefix to prepend to the start of the string.
5661     * @param ignoreCase Indicates whether the compare should ignore case.
5662     * @param prefixes Additional prefixes that are valid (optional).
5663     *
5664     * @return A new String if prefix was prepended, the same string otherwise.
5665     */
5666    private static String prependIfMissing(final String str, final CharSequence prefix, final boolean ignoreCase, final CharSequence... prefixes) {
5667        if (str == null || isEmpty(prefix) || startsWith(str, prefix, ignoreCase)) {
5668            return str;
5669        }
5670        if (ArrayUtils.isNotEmpty(prefixes)) {
5671            for (final CharSequence p : prefixes) {
5672                if (startsWith(str, p, ignoreCase)) {
5673                    return str;
5674                }
5675            }
5676        }
5677        return prefix.toString() + str;
5678    }
5679
5680    /**
5681     * Prepends the prefix to the start of the string if the string does not
5682     * already start with any of the prefixes.
5683     *
5684     * <pre>
5685     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing(null, null) = null
5686     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("abc", null) = "abc"
5687     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("", "xyz") = "xyz"
5688     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("abc", "xyz") = "xyzabc"
5689     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("xyzabc", "xyz") = "xyzabc"
5690     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("XYZabc", "xyz") = "xyzXYZabc"
5691     * </pre>
5692     * <p>With additional prefixes,</p>
5693     * <pre>
5694     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing(null, null, null) = null
5695     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("abc", null, null) = "abc"
5696     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("", "xyz", null) = "xyz"
5697     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("abc", "xyz", new CharSequence[]{null}) = "xyzabc"
5698     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("abc", "xyz", "") = "abc"
5699     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("abc", "xyz", "mno") = "xyzabc"
5700     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("xyzabc", "xyz", "mno") = "xyzabc"
5701     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("mnoabc", "xyz", "mno") = "mnoabc"
5702     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("XYZabc", "xyz", "mno") = "xyzXYZabc"
5703     * StringUtils.prependIfMissing("MNOabc", "xyz", "mno") = "xyzMNOabc"
5704     * </pre>
5705     *
5706     * @param str The string.
5707     * @param prefix The prefix to prepend to the start of the string.
5708     * @param prefixes Additional prefixes that are valid.
5709     *
5710     * @return A new String if prefix was prepended, the same string otherwise.
5711     *
5712     * @since 3.2
5713     */
5714    public static String prependIfMissing(final String str, final CharSequence prefix, final CharSequence... prefixes) {
5715        return prependIfMissing(str, prefix, false, prefixes);
5716    }

5718    /**
5719     * Prepends the prefix to the start of the string if the string does not
5720     * already start, case-insensitive, with any of the prefixes.
5721     *
5722     * <pre>
5723     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase(null, null) = null
5724     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("abc", null) = "abc"
5725     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("", "xyz") = "xyz"
5726     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("abc", "xyz") = "xyzabc"
5727     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("xyzabc", "xyz") = "xyzabc"
5728     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("XYZabc", "xyz") = "XYZabc"
5729     * </pre>
5730     * <p>With additional prefixes,</p>
5731     * <pre>
5732     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase(null, null, null) = null
5733     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("abc", null, null) = "abc"
5734     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("", "xyz", null) = "xyz"
5735     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("abc", "xyz", new CharSequence[]{null}) = "xyzabc"
5736     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("abc", "xyz", "") = "abc"
5737     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("abc", "xyz", "mno") = "xyzabc"
5738     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("xyzabc", "xyz", "mno") = "xyzabc"
5739     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("mnoabc", "xyz", "mno") = "mnoabc"
5740     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("XYZabc", "xyz", "mno") = "XYZabc"
5741     * StringUtils.prependIfMissingIgnoreCase("MNOabc", "xyz", "mno") = "MNOabc"
5742     * </pre>
5743     *
5744     * @param str The string.
5745     * @param prefix The prefix to prepend to the start of the string.
5746     * @param prefixes Additional prefixes that are valid (optional).
5747     *
5748     * @return A new String if prefix was prepended, the same string otherwise.
5749     *
5750     * @since 3.2
5751     */
5752    public static String prependIfMissingIgnoreCase(final String str, final CharSequence prefix, final CharSequence... prefixes) {
5753        return prependIfMissing(str, prefix, true, prefixes);
5754    }
5755
5756    /**
5757     * Removes all occurrences of a character from within the source string.
5758     *
5759     * <p>A {@code null} source string will return {@code null}.
5760     * An empty ("") source string will return the empty string.</p>
5761     *
5762     * <pre>
5763     * StringUtils.remove(null, *)       = null
5764     * StringUtils.remove("", *)         = ""
5765     * StringUtils.remove("queued", 'u') = "qeed"
5766     * StringUtils.remove("queued", 'z') = "queued"
5767     * </pre>
5768     *
5769     * @param str  the source String to search, may be null
5770     * @param remove  the char to search for and remove, may be null
5771     * @return the substring with the char removed if found,
5772     *  {@code null} if null String input
5773     * @since 2.1
5774     */
5775    public static String remove(final String str, final char remove) {
5776        if (isEmpty(str) || str.indexOf(remove) == INDEX_NOT_FOUND) {
5777            return str;
5778        }
5779        final char[] chars = str.toCharArray();
5780        int pos = 0;
5781        for (int i = 0; i < chars.length; i++) {
5782            if (chars[i] != remove) {
5783                chars[pos++] = chars[i];
5784            }
5785        }
5786        return new String(chars, 0, pos);
5787    }
5788
5789    /**
5790     * Removes all occurrences of a substring from within the source string.
5791     *
5792     * <p>A {@code null} source string will return {@code null}.
5793     * An empty ("") source string will return the empty string.
5794     * A {@code null} remove string will return the source string.
5795     * An empty ("") remove string will return the source string.</p>
5796     *
5797     * <pre>
5798     * StringUtils.remove(null, *)        = null
5799     * StringUtils.remove("", *)          = ""
5800     * StringUtils.remove(*, null)        = *
5801     * StringUtils.remove(*, "")          = *
5802     * StringUtils.remove("queued", "ue") = "qd"
5803     * StringUtils.remove("queued", "zz") = "queued"
5804     * </pre>
5805     *
5806     * @param str  the source String to search, may be null
5807     * @param remove  the String to search for and remove, may be null
5808     * @return the substring with the string removed if found,
5809     *  {@code null} if null String input
5810     * @since 2.1
5811     */
5812    public static String remove(final String str, final String remove) {
5813        if (isEmpty(str) || isEmpty(remove)) {
5814            return str;
5815        }
5816        return replace(str, remove, EMPTY, -1);
5817    }
5818
5819    /**
5820     * Removes each substring of the text String that matches the given regular expression.
5821     *
5822     * This method is a {@code null} safe equivalent to:
5823     * <ul>
5824     *  <li>{@code text.replaceAll(regex, StringUtils.EMPTY)}</li>
5825     *  <li>{@code Pattern.compile(regex).matcher(text).replaceAll(StringUtils.EMPTY)}</li>
5826     * </ul>
5827     *
5828     * <p>A {@code null} reference passed to this method is a no-op.</p>
5829     *
5830     * <p>Unlike in the {@link #removePattern(String, String)} method, the {@link Pattern#DOTALL} option
5831     * is NOT automatically added.
5832     * To use the DOTALL option prepend {@code "(?s)"} to the regex.
5833     * DOTALL is also known as single-line mode in Perl.</p>
5834     *
5835     * <pre>
5836     * StringUtils.removeAll(null, *)      = null
5837     * StringUtils.removeAll("any", (String) null)  = "any"
5838     * StringUtils.removeAll("any", "")    = "any"
5839     * StringUtils.removeAll("any", ".*")  = ""
5840     * StringUtils.removeAll("any", ".+")  = ""
5841     * StringUtils.removeAll("abc", ".?")  = ""
5842     * StringUtils.removeAll("A&lt;__&gt;\n&lt;__&gt;B", "&lt;.*&gt;")      = "A\nB"
5843     * StringUtils.removeAll("A&lt;__&gt;\n&lt;__&gt;B", "(?s)&lt;.*&gt;")  = "AB"
5844     * StringUtils.removeAll("ABCabc123abc", "[a-z]")     = "ABC123"
5845     * </pre>
5846     *
5847     * @param text  text to remove from, may be null
5848     * @param regex  the regular expression to which this string is to be matched
5849     * @return  the text with any removes processed,
5850     *              {@code null} if null String input
5851     *
5852     * @throws  java.util.regex.PatternSyntaxException
5853     *              if the regular expression's syntax is invalid
5854     *
5855     * @see #replaceAll(String, String, String)
5856     * @see #removePattern(String, String)
5857     * @see String#replaceAll(String, String)
5858     * @see java.util.regex.Pattern
5859     * @see java.util.regex.Pattern#DOTALL
5860     * @since 3.5
5861     *
5862     * @deprecated Moved to RegExUtils.
5863     */
5864    @Deprecated
5865    public static String removeAll(final String text, final String regex) {
5866        return RegExUtils.removeAll(text, regex);
5867    }
5868
5869    /**
5870     * Removes a substring only if it is at the end of a source string,
5871     * otherwise returns the source string.
5872     *
5873     * <p>A {@code null} source string will return {@code null}.
5874     * An empty ("") source string will return the empty string.
5875     * A {@code null} search string will return the source string.</p>
5876     *
5877     * <pre>
5878     * StringUtils.removeEnd(null, *)      = null
5879     * StringUtils.removeEnd("", *)        = ""
5880     * StringUtils.removeEnd(*, null)      = *
5881     * StringUtils.removeEnd("www.domain.com", ".com.")  = "www.domain.com"
5882     * StringUtils.removeEnd("www.domain.com", ".com")   = "www.domain"
5883     * StringUtils.removeEnd("www.domain.com", "domain") = "www.domain.com"
5884     * StringUtils.removeEnd("abc", "")    = "abc"
5885     * </pre>
5886     *
5887     * @param str  the source String to search, may be null
5888     * @param remove  the String to search for and remove, may be null
5889     * @return the substring with the string removed if found,
5890     *  {@code null} if null String input
5891     * @since 2.1
5892     */
5893    public static String removeEnd(final String str, final String remove) {
5894        if (isEmpty(str) || isEmpty(remove)) {
5895            return str;
5896        }
5897        if (str.endsWith(remove)) {
5898            return str.substring(0, str.length() - remove.length());
5899        }
5900        return str;
5901    }

5903    /**
5904     * Case insensitive removal of a substring if it is at the end of a source string,
5905     * otherwise returns the source string.
5906     *
5907     * <p>A {@code null} source string will return {@code null}.
5908     * An empty ("") source string will return the empty string.
5909     * A {@code null} search string will return the source string.</p>
5910     *
5911     * <pre>
5912     * StringUtils.removeEndIgnoreCase(null, *)      = null
5913     * StringUtils.removeEndIgnoreCase("", *)        = ""
5914     * StringUtils.removeEndIgnoreCase(*, null)      = *
5915     * StringUtils.removeEndIgnoreCase("www.domain.com", ".com.")  = "www.domain.com"
5916     * StringUtils.removeEndIgnoreCase("www.domain.com", ".com")   = "www.domain"
5917     * StringUtils.removeEndIgnoreCase("www.domain.com", "domain") = "www.domain.com"
5918     * StringUtils.removeEndIgnoreCase("abc", "")    = "abc"
5919     * StringUtils.removeEndIgnoreCase("www.domain.com", ".COM") = "www.domain")
5920     * StringUtils.removeEndIgnoreCase("www.domain.COM", ".com") = "www.domain")
5921     * </pre>
5922     *
5923     * @param str  the source String to search, may be null
5924     * @param remove  the String to search for (case-insensitive) and remove, may be null
5925     * @return the substring with the string removed if found,
5926     *  {@code null} if null String input
5927     * @since 2.4
5928     */
5929    public static String removeEndIgnoreCase(final String str, final String remove) {
5930        if (isEmpty(str) || isEmpty(remove)) {
5931            return str;
5932        }
5933        if (endsWithIgnoreCase(str, remove)) {
5934            return str.substring(0, str.length() - remove.length());
5935        }
5936        return str;
5937    }
