7764    /**
7765     * Splits the provided text into an array with a maximum length,
7766     * separators specified, preserving all tokens, including empty tokens
7767     * created by adjacent separators.
7768     *
7769     * <p>The separator is not included in the returned String array.
7770     * Adjacent separators are treated as separators for empty tokens.
7771     * Adjacent separators are treated as one separator.</p>
7772     *
7773     * <p>A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.
7774     * A {@code null} separatorChars splits on whitespace.</p>
7775     *
7776     * <p>If more than {@code max} delimited substrings are found, the last
7777     * returned string includes all characters after the first {@code max - 1}
7778     * returned strings (including separator characters).</p>
7779     *
7780     * <pre>
7781     * StringUtils.splitPreserveAllTokens(null, *, *)            = null
7782     * StringUtils.splitPreserveAllTokens("", *, *)              = []
7783     * StringUtils.splitPreserveAllTokens("ab de fg", null, 0)   = ["ab", "de", "fg"]
7784     * StringUtils.splitPreserveAllTokens("ab   de fg", null, 0) = ["ab", "", "", "de", "fg"]
7785     * StringUtils.splitPreserveAllTokens("ab:cd:ef", ":", 0)    = ["ab", "cd", "ef"]
7786     * StringUtils.splitPreserveAllTokens("ab:cd:ef", ":", 2)    = ["ab", "cd:ef"]
7787     * StringUtils.splitPreserveAllTokens("ab   de fg", null, 2) = ["ab", "  de fg"]
7788     * StringUtils.splitPreserveAllTokens("ab   de fg", null, 3) = ["ab", "", " de fg"]
7789     * StringUtils.splitPreserveAllTokens("ab   de fg", null, 4) = ["ab", "", "", "de fg"]
7790     * </pre>
7791     *
7792     * @param str  the String to parse, may be {@code null}
7793     * @param separatorChars  the characters used as the delimiters,
7794     *  {@code null} splits on whitespace
7795     * @param max  the maximum number of elements to include in the
7796     *  array. A zero or negative value implies no limit
7797     * @return an array of parsed Strings, {@code null} if null String input
7798     * @since 2.1
7799     */
7800    public static String[] splitPreserveAllTokens(final String str, final String separatorChars, final int max) {
7801        return splitWorker(str, separatorChars, max, true);
7802    }
7803
7804    /**
7805     * Performs the logic for the {@code split} and
7806     * {@code splitPreserveAllTokens} methods that do not return a
7807     * maximum array length.
7808     *
7809     * @param str  the String to parse, may be {@code null}
7810     * @param separatorChar the separate character
7811     * @param preserveAllTokens if {@code true}, adjacent separators are
7812     * treated as empty token separators; if {@code false}, adjacent
7813     * separators are treated as one separator.
7814     * @return an array of parsed Strings, {@code null} if null String input
7815     */
7816    private static String[] splitWorker(final String str, final char separatorChar, final boolean preserveAllTokens) {
7817        // Performance tuned for 2.0 (JDK1.4)
7818
7819        if (str == null) {
7820            return null;
7821        }
7822        final int len = str.length();
7823        if (len == 0) {
7824            return ArrayUtils.EMPTY_STRING_ARRAY;
7825        }
7826        final List<String> list = new ArrayList<>();
7827        int i = 0;
7828        int start = 0;
7829        boolean match = false;
7830        boolean lastMatch = false;
7831        while (i < len) {
7832            if (str.charAt(i) == separatorChar) {
7833                if (match || preserveAllTokens) {
7834                    list.add(str.substring(start, i));
7835                    match = false;
7836                    lastMatch = true;
7837                }
7838                start = ++i;
7839                continue;
7840            }
7841            lastMatch = false;
7842            match = true;
7843            i++;
7844        }
7845        if (match || preserveAllTokens && lastMatch) {
7846            list.add(str.substring(start, i));
7847        }
7848        return list.toArray(ArrayUtils.EMPTY_STRING_ARRAY);
7849    }
7850
7851    /**
7852     * Performs the logic for the {@code split} and
7853     * {@code splitPreserveAllTokens} methods that return a maximum array
7854     * length.
7855     *
7856     * @param str  the String to parse, may be {@code null}
7857     * @param separatorChars the separate character
7858     * @param max  the maximum number of elements to include in the
7859     *  array. A zero or negative value implies no limit.
7860     * @param preserveAllTokens if {@code true}, adjacent separators are
7861     * treated as empty token separators; if {@code false}, adjacent
7862     * separators are treated as one separator.
7863     * @return an array of parsed Strings, {@code null} if null String input
7864     */
7865    private static String[] splitWorker(final String str, final String separatorChars, final int max, final boolean preserveAllTokens) {
7866        // Performance tuned for 2.0 (JDK1.4)
7867        // Direct code is quicker than StringTokenizer.
7868        // Also, StringTokenizer uses isSpace() not isWhitespace()
7869
7870        if (str == null) {
7871            return null;
7872        }
7873        final int len = str.length();
7874        if (len == 0) {
7875            return ArrayUtils.EMPTY_STRING_ARRAY;
7876        }
7877        final List<String> list = new ArrayList<>();
7878        int sizePlus1 = 1;
7879        int i = 0;
7880        int start = 0;
7881        boolean match = false;
7882        boolean lastMatch = false;
7883        if (separatorChars == null) {
7884            // Null separator means use whitespace
7885            while (i < len) {
7886                if (Character.isWhitespace(str.charAt(i))) {
7887                    if (match || preserveAllTokens) {
7888                        lastMatch = true;
7889                        if (sizePlus1++ == max) {
7890                            i = len;
7891                            lastMatch = false;
7892                        }
7893                        list.add(str.substring(start, i));
7894                        match = false;
7895                    }
7896                    start = ++i;
7897                    continue;
7898                }
7899                lastMatch = false;
7900                match = true;
7901                i++;
7902            }
7903        } else if (separatorChars.length() == 1) {
7904            // Optimise 1 character case
7905            final char sep = separatorChars.charAt(0);
7906            while (i < len) {
7907                if (str.charAt(i) == sep) {
7908                    if (match || preserveAllTokens) {
7909                        lastMatch = true;
7910                        if (sizePlus1++ == max) {
7911                            i = len;
7912                            lastMatch = false;
7913                        }
7914                        list.add(str.substring(start, i));
7915                        match = false;
7916                    }
7917                    start = ++i;
7918                    continue;
7919                }
7920                lastMatch = false;
7921                match = true;
7922                i++;
7923            }
7924        } else {
7925            // standard case
7926            while (i < len) {
7927                if (separatorChars.indexOf(str.charAt(i)) >= 0) {
7928                    if (match || preserveAllTokens) {
7929                        lastMatch = true;
7930                        if (sizePlus1++ == max) {
7931                            i = len;
7932                            lastMatch = false;
7933                        }
7934                        list.add(str.substring(start, i));
7935                        match = false;
7936                    }
7937                    start = ++i;
7938                    continue;
7939                }
7940                lastMatch = false;
7941                match = true;
7942                i++;
7943            }
7944        }
7945        if (match || preserveAllTokens && lastMatch) {
7946            list.add(str.substring(start, i));
7947        }
7948        return list.toArray(ArrayUtils.EMPTY_STRING_ARRAY);
7949    }
7950
7951    /**
7952     * Check if a CharSequence starts with a specified prefix.
7953     *
7954     * <p>{@code null}s are handled without exceptions. Two {@code null}
7955     * references are considered to be equal. The comparison is case-sensitive.</p>
7956     *
7957     * <pre>
7958     * StringUtils.startsWith(null, null)      = true
7959     * StringUtils.startsWith(null, "abc")     = false
7960     * StringUtils.startsWith("abcdef", null)  = false
7961     * StringUtils.startsWith("abcdef", "abc") = true
7962     * StringUtils.startsWith("ABCDEF", "abc") = false
7963     * </pre>
7964     *
7965     * @see String#startsWith(String)
7966     * @param str  the CharSequence to check, may be null
7967     * @param prefix the prefix to find, may be null
7968     * @return {@code true} if the CharSequence starts with the prefix, case-sensitive, or
7969     *  both {@code null}
7970     * @since 2.4
7971     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from startsWith(String, String) to startsWith(CharSequence, CharSequence)
7972     */
7973    public static boolean startsWith(final CharSequence str, final CharSequence prefix) {
7974        return startsWith(str, prefix, false);
7975    }
7976
7977    /**
7978     * Check if a CharSequence starts with a specified prefix (optionally case insensitive).
7979     *
7980     * @see String#startsWith(String)
7981     * @param str  the CharSequence to check, may be null
7982     * @param prefix the prefix to find, may be null
7983     * @param ignoreCase indicates whether the compare should ignore case
7984     *  (case-insensitive) or not.
7985     * @return {@code true} if the CharSequence starts with the prefix or
7986     *  both {@code null}
7987     */
7988    private static boolean startsWith(final CharSequence str, final CharSequence prefix, final boolean ignoreCase) {
7989        if (str == null || prefix == null) {
7990            return str == prefix;
7991        }
7992        // Get length once instead of twice in the unlikely case that it changes.
7993        final int preLen = prefix.length();
7994        if (preLen > str.length()) {
7995            return false;
7996        }
7997        return CharSequenceUtils.regionMatches(str, ignoreCase, 0, prefix, 0, preLen);
7998    }
7999
8000    /**
8001     * Check if a CharSequence starts with any of the provided case-sensitive prefixes.
8002     *
8003     * <pre>
8004     * StringUtils.startsWithAny(null, null)      = false
8005     * StringUtils.startsWithAny(null, new String[] {"abc"})  = false
8006     * StringUtils.startsWithAny("abcxyz", null)     = false
8007     * StringUtils.startsWithAny("abcxyz", new String[] {""}) = true
8008     * StringUtils.startsWithAny("abcxyz", new String[] {"abc"}) = true
8009     * StringUtils.startsWithAny("abcxyz", new String[] {null, "xyz", "abc"}) = true
8010     * StringUtils.startsWithAny("abcxyz", null, "xyz", "ABCX") = false
8011     * StringUtils.startsWithAny("ABCXYZ", null, "xyz", "abc") = false
8012     * </pre>
8013     *
8014     * @param sequence the CharSequence to check, may be null
8015     * @param searchStrings the case-sensitive CharSequence prefixes, may be empty or contain {@code null}
8016     * @see StringUtils#startsWith(CharSequence, CharSequence)
8017     * @return {@code true} if the input {@code sequence} is {@code null} AND no {@code searchStrings} are provided, or
8018     *   the input {@code sequence} begins with any of the provided case-sensitive {@code searchStrings}.
8019     * @since 2.5
8020     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from startsWithAny(String, String[]) to startsWithAny(CharSequence, CharSequence...)
8021     */
8022    public static boolean startsWithAny(final CharSequence sequence, final CharSequence... searchStrings) {
8023        if (isEmpty(sequence) || ArrayUtils.isEmpty(searchStrings)) {
8024            return false;
8025        }
8026        for (final CharSequence searchString : searchStrings) {
8027            if (startsWith(sequence, searchString)) {
8028                return true;
8029            }
8030        }
8031        return false;
8032    }
8033
8034    /**
8035     * Case insensitive check if a CharSequence starts with a specified prefix.
8036     *
8037     * <p>{@code null}s are handled without exceptions. Two {@code null}
8038     * references are considered to be equal. The comparison is case insensitive.</p>
8039     *
8040     * <pre>
8041     * StringUtils.startsWithIgnoreCase(null, null)      = true
8042     * StringUtils.startsWithIgnoreCase(null, "abc")     = false
8043     * StringUtils.startsWithIgnoreCase("abcdef", null)  = false
8044     * StringUtils.startsWithIgnoreCase("abcdef", "abc") = true
8045     * StringUtils.startsWithIgnoreCase("ABCDEF", "abc") = true
8046     * </pre>
8047     *
8048     * @see String#startsWith(String)
8049     * @param str  the CharSequence to check, may be null
8050     * @param prefix the prefix to find, may be null
8051     * @return {@code true} if the CharSequence starts with the prefix, case-insensitive, or
8052     *  both {@code null}
8053     * @since 2.4
8054     * @since 3.0 Changed signature from startsWithIgnoreCase(String, String) to startsWithIgnoreCase(CharSequence, CharSequence)
8055     */
8056    public static boolean startsWithIgnoreCase(final CharSequence str, final CharSequence prefix) {
8057        return startsWith(str, prefix, true);
8058    }
8059
8060    /**
8061     * Strips whitespace from the start and end of a String.
8062     *
8063     * <p>This is similar to {@link #trim(String)} but removes whitespace.
8064     * Whitespace is defined by {@link Character#isWhitespace(char)}.</p>
8065     *
8066     * <p>A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.</p>
8067     *
8068     * <pre>
8069     * StringUtils.strip(null)     = null
8070     * StringUtils.strip("")       = ""
8071     * StringUtils.strip("   ")    = ""
8072     * StringUtils.strip("abc")    = "abc"
8073     * StringUtils.strip("  abc")  = "abc"
8074     * StringUtils.strip("abc  ")  = "abc"
8075     * StringUtils.strip(" abc ")  = "abc"
8076     * StringUtils.strip(" ab c ") = "ab c"
8077     * </pre>
8078     *
8079     * @param str  the String to remove whitespace from, may be null
8080     * @return the stripped String, {@code null} if null String input
8081     */
8082    public static String strip(final String str) {
8083        return strip(str, null);
8084    }
8085
8086    /**
8087     * Strips any of a set of characters from the start and end of a String.
8088     * This is similar to {@link String#trim()} but allows the characters
8089     * to be stripped to be controlled.
8090     *
8091     * <p>A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.
8092     * An empty string ("") input returns the empty string.</p>
8093     *
8094     * <p>If the stripChars String is {@code null}, whitespace is
8095     * stripped as defined by {@link Character#isWhitespace(char)}.
8096     * Alternatively use {@link #strip(String)}.</p>
8097     *
8098     * <pre>
8099     * StringUtils.strip(null, *)          = null
8100     * StringUtils.strip("", *)            = ""
8101     * StringUtils.strip("abc", null)      = "abc"
8102     * StringUtils.strip("  abc", null)    = "abc"
8103     * StringUtils.strip("abc  ", null)    = "abc"
8104     * StringUtils.strip(" abc ", null)    = "abc"
8105     * StringUtils.strip("  abcyx", "xyz") = "  abc"
8106     * </pre>
8107     *
8108     * @param str  the String to remove characters from, may be null
8109     * @param stripChars  the characters to remove, null treated as whitespace
8110     * @return the stripped String, {@code null} if null String input
8111     */
8112    public static String strip(String str, final String stripChars) {
8113        str = stripStart(str, stripChars);
8114        return stripEnd(str, stripChars);
8115    }
8116
8117    /**
8118     * Removes diacritics (~= accents) from a string. The case will not be altered.
8119     * <p>For instance, '&agrave;' will be replaced by 'a'.</p>
8120     * <p>Note that ligatures will be left as is.</p>
8121     *
8122     * <pre>
8123     * StringUtils.stripAccents(null)                = null
8124     * StringUtils.stripAccents("")                  = ""
8125     * StringUtils.stripAccents("control")           = "control"
8126     * StringUtils.stripAccents("&eacute;clair")     = "eclair"
8127     * </pre>
8128     *
8129     * @param input String to be stripped
8130     * @return input text with diacritics removed
8131     *
8132     * @since 3.0
8133     */
8134    // See also Lucene's ASCIIFoldingFilter (Lucene 2.9) that replaces accented characters by their unaccented equivalent (and uncommitted bug fix: https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/LUCENE-1343?focusedCommentId=12858907&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels%3Acomment-tabpanel#action_12858907).
8135    public static String stripAccents(final String input) {
8136        if (input == null) {
8137            return null;
8138        }
8139        final StringBuilder decomposed = new StringBuilder(Normalizer.normalize(input, Normalizer.Form.NFD));
8140        convertRemainingAccentCharacters(decomposed);
8141        // Note that this doesn't correctly remove ligatures...
8142        return STRIP_ACCENTS_PATTERN.matcher(decomposed).replaceAll(EMPTY);
8143    }
8144
8145    /**
8146     * Strips whitespace from the start and end of every String in an array.
8147     * Whitespace is defined by {@link Character#isWhitespace(char)}.
8148     *
8149     * <p>A new array is returned each time, except for length zero.
8150     * A {@code null} array will return {@code null}.
8151     * An empty array will return itself.
8152     * A {@code null} array entry will be ignored.</p>
8153     *
8154     * <pre>
8155     * StringUtils.stripAll(null)             = null
8156     * StringUtils.stripAll([])               = []
8157     * StringUtils.stripAll(["abc", "  abc"]) = ["abc", "abc"]
8158     * StringUtils.stripAll(["abc  ", null])  = ["abc", null]
8159     * </pre>
8160     *
8161     * @param strs  the array to remove whitespace from, may be null
8162     * @return the stripped Strings, {@code null} if null array input
8163     */
8164    public static String[] stripAll(final String... strs) {
8165        return stripAll(strs, null);
8166    }
8167
8168    /**
8169     * Strips any of a set of characters from the start and end of every
8170     * String in an array.
8171     * <p>Whitespace is defined by {@link Character#isWhitespace(char)}.</p>
8172     *
8173     * <p>A new array is returned each time, except for length zero.
8174     * A {@code null} array will return {@code null}.
8175     * An empty array will return itself.
8176     * A {@code null} array entry will be ignored.
8177     * A {@code null} stripChars will strip whitespace as defined by
8178     * {@link Character#isWhitespace(char)}.</p>
8179     *
8180     * <pre>
8181     * StringUtils.stripAll(null, *)                = null
8182     * StringUtils.stripAll([], *)                  = []
8183     * StringUtils.stripAll(["abc", "  abc"], null) = ["abc", "abc"]
8184     * StringUtils.stripAll(["abc  ", null], null)  = ["abc", null]
8185     * StringUtils.stripAll(["abc  ", null], "yz")  = ["abc  ", null]
8186     * StringUtils.stripAll(["yabcz", null], "yz")  = ["abc", null]
8187     * </pre>
8188     *
8189     * @param strs  the array to remove characters from, may be null
8190     * @param stripChars  the characters to remove, null treated as whitespace
8191     * @return the stripped Strings, {@code null} if null array input
8192     */
8193    public static String[] stripAll(final String[] strs, final String stripChars) {
8194        final int strsLen = ArrayUtils.getLength(strs);
8195        if (strsLen == 0) {
8196            return strs;
8197        }
8198        final String[] newArr = new String[strsLen];
8199        Arrays.setAll(newArr, i -> strip(strs[i], stripChars));
8200        return newArr;
8201    }
8202
8203    /**
8204     * Strips any of a set of characters from the end of a String.
8205     *
8206     * <p>A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.
8207     * An empty string ("") input returns the empty string.</p>
8208     *
8209     * <p>If the stripChars String is {@code null}, whitespace is
8210     * stripped as defined by {@link Character#isWhitespace(char)}.</p>
8211     *
8212     * <pre>
8213     * StringUtils.stripEnd(null, *)          = null
8214     * StringUtils.stripEnd("", *)            = ""
8215     * StringUtils.stripEnd("abc", "")        = "abc"
8216     * StringUtils.stripEnd("abc", null)      = "abc"
8217     * StringUtils.stripEnd("  abc", null)    = "  abc"
8218     * StringUtils.stripEnd("abc  ", null)    = "abc"
8219     * StringUtils.stripEnd(" abc ", null)    = " abc"
8220     * StringUtils.stripEnd("  abcyx", "xyz") = "  abc"
8221     * StringUtils.stripEnd("120.00", ".0")   = "12"
8222     * </pre>
8223     *
8224     * @param str  the String to remove characters from, may be null
8225     * @param stripChars  the set of characters to remove, null treated as whitespace
8226     * @return the stripped String, {@code null} if null String input
8227     */
8228    public static String stripEnd(final String str, final String stripChars) {
8229        int end = length(str);
8230        if (end == 0) {
8231            return str;
8232        }
8233
8234        if (stripChars == null) {
8235            while (end != 0 && Character.isWhitespace(str.charAt(end - 1))) {
8236                end--;
8237            }
8238        } else if (stripChars.isEmpty()) {
8239            return str;
8240        } else {
8241            while (end != 0 && stripChars.indexOf(str.charAt(end - 1)) != INDEX_NOT_FOUND) {
8242                end--;
8243            }
8244        }
8245        return str.substring(0, end);
8246    }
8247
8248    /**
8249     * Strips any of a set of characters from the start of a String.
8250     *
8251     * <p>A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.
8252     * An empty string ("") input returns the empty string.</p>
8253     *
8254     * <p>If the stripChars String is {@code null}, whitespace is
8255     * stripped as defined by {@link Character#isWhitespace(char)}.</p>
8256     *
8257     * <pre>
8258     * StringUtils.stripStart(null, *)          = null
8259     * StringUtils.stripStart("", *)            = ""
8260     * StringUtils.stripStart("abc", "")        = "abc"
8261     * StringUtils.stripStart("abc", null)      = "abc"
8262     * StringUtils.stripStart("  abc", null)    = "abc"
8263     * StringUtils.stripStart("abc  ", null)    = "abc  "
8264     * StringUtils.stripStart(" abc ", null)    = "abc "
8265     * StringUtils.stripStart("yxabc  ", "xyz") = "abc  "
8266     * </pre>
8267     *
8268     * @param str  the String to remove characters from, may be null
8269     * @param stripChars  the characters to remove, null treated as whitespace
8270     * @return the stripped String, {@code null} if null String input
8271     */
8272    public static String stripStart(final String str, final String stripChars) {
8273        final int strLen = length(str);
8274        if (strLen == 0) {
8275            return str;
8276        }
8277        int start = 0;
8278        if (stripChars == null) {
8279            while (start != strLen && Character.isWhitespace(str.charAt(start))) {
8280                start++;
8281            }
8282        } else if (stripChars.isEmpty()) {
8283            return str;
8284        } else {
8285            while (start != strLen && stripChars.indexOf(str.charAt(start)) != INDEX_NOT_FOUND) {
8286                start++;
8287            }
8288        }
8289        return str.substring(start);
8290    }
8291
8292    /**
8293     * Strips whitespace from the start and end of a String  returning
8294     * an empty String if {@code null} input.
8295     *
8296     * <p>This is similar to {@link #trimToEmpty(String)} but removes whitespace.
8297     * Whitespace is defined by {@link Character#isWhitespace(char)}.</p>
8298     *
8299     * <pre>
8300     * StringUtils.stripToEmpty(null)     = ""
8301     * StringUtils.stripToEmpty("")       = ""
8302     * StringUtils.stripToEmpty("   ")    = ""
8303     * StringUtils.stripToEmpty("abc")    = "abc"
8304     * StringUtils.stripToEmpty("  abc")  = "abc"
8305     * StringUtils.stripToEmpty("abc  ")  = "abc"
8306     * StringUtils.stripToEmpty(" abc ")  = "abc"
8307     * StringUtils.stripToEmpty(" ab c ") = "ab c"
8308     * </pre>
8309     *
8310     * @param str  the String to be stripped, may be null
8311     * @return the trimmed String, or an empty String if {@code null} input
8312     * @since 2.0
8313     */
8314    public static String stripToEmpty(final String str) {
8315        return str == null ? EMPTY : strip(str, null);
8316    }
8317
8318    /**
8319     * Strips whitespace from the start and end of a String  returning
8320     * {@code null} if the String is empty ("") after the strip.
8321     *
8322     * <p>This is similar to {@link #trimToNull(String)} but removes whitespace.
8323     * Whitespace is defined by {@link Character#isWhitespace(char)}.</p>
8324     *
8325     * <pre>
8326     * StringUtils.stripToNull(null)     = null
8327     * StringUtils.stripToNull("")       = null
8328     * StringUtils.stripToNull("   ")    = null
8329     * StringUtils.stripToNull("abc")    = "abc"
8330     * StringUtils.stripToNull("  abc")  = "abc"
8331     * StringUtils.stripToNull("abc  ")  = "abc"
8332     * StringUtils.stripToNull(" abc ")  = "abc"
8333     * StringUtils.stripToNull(" ab c ") = "ab c"
8334     * </pre>
8335     *
8336     * @param str  the String to be stripped, may be null
8337     * @return the stripped String,
8338     *  {@code null} if whitespace, empty or null String input
8339     * @since 2.0
8340     */
8341    public static String stripToNull(String str) {
8342        if (str == null) {
8343            return null;
8344        }
8345        str = strip(str, null);
8346        return str.isEmpty() ? null : str; // NOSONARLINT str cannot be null here
8347    }
8348
8349    /**
8350     * Gets a substring from the specified String avoiding exceptions.
8351     *
8352     * <p>A negative start position can be used to start {@code n}
8353     * characters from the end of the String.</p>
8354     *
8355     * <p>A {@code null} String will return {@code null}.
8356     * An empty ("") String will return "".</p>
8357     *
8358     * <pre>
8359     * StringUtils.substring(null, *)   = null
8360     * StringUtils.substring("", *)     = ""
8361     * StringUtils.substring("abc", 0)  = "abc"
8362     * StringUtils.substring("abc", 2)  = "c"
8363     * StringUtils.substring("abc", 4)  = ""
8364     * StringUtils.substring("abc", -2) = "bc"
8365     * StringUtils.substring("abc", -4) = "abc"
8366     * </pre>
8367     *
8368     * @param str  the String to get the substring from, may be null
8369     * @param start  the position to start from, negative means
8370     *  count back from the end of the String by this many characters
8371     * @return substring from start position, {@code null} if null String input
8372     */
8373    public static String substring(final String str, int start) {
8374        if (str == null) {
8375            return null;
8376        }
8377
8378        // handle negatives, which means last n characters
8379        if (start < 0) {
8380            start = str.length() + start; // remember start is negative
8381        }
8382
8383        if (start < 0) {
8384            start = 0;
8385        }
8386        if (start > str.length()) {
8387            return EMPTY;
8388        }
8389
8390        return str.substring(start);
8391    }
8392
8393    /**
8394     * Gets a substring from the specified String avoiding exceptions.
8395     *
8396     * <p>A negative start position can be used to start/end {@code n}
8397     * characters from the end of the String.</p>
8398     *
8399     * <p>The returned substring starts with the character in the {@code start}
8400     * position and ends before the {@code end} position. All position counting is
8401     * zero-based -- i.e., to start at the beginning of the string use
8402     * {@code start = 0}. Negative start and end positions can be used to
8403     * specify offsets relative to the end of the String.</p>
8404     *
8405     * <p>If {@code start} is not strictly to the left of {@code end}, ""
8406     * is returned.</p>
8407     *
8408     * <pre>
8409     * StringUtils.substring(null, *, *)    = null
8410     * StringUtils.substring("", * ,  *)    = "";
8411     * StringUtils.substring("abc", 0, 2)   = "ab"
8412     * StringUtils.substring("abc", 2, 0)   = ""
8413     * StringUtils.substring("abc", 2, 4)   = "c"
8414     * StringUtils.substring("abc", 4, 6)   = ""
8415     * StringUtils.substring("abc", 2, 2)   = ""
8416     * StringUtils.substring("abc", -2, -1) = "b"
8417     * StringUtils.substring("abc", -4, 2)  = "ab"
8418     * </pre>
8419     *
8420     * @param str  the String to get the substring from, may be null
8421     * @param start  the position to start from, negative means
8422     *  count back from the end of the String by this many characters
8423     * @param end  the position to end at (exclusive), negative means
8424     *  count back from the end of the String by this many characters
8425     * @return substring from start position to end position,
8426     *  {@code null} if null String input
8427     */
8428    public static String substring(final String str, int start, int end) {
8429        if (str == null) {
8430            return null;
8431        }
8432
8433        // handle negatives
8434        if (end < 0) {
8435            end = str.length() + end; // remember end is negative
8436        }
8437        if (start < 0) {
8438            start = str.length() + start; // remember start is negative
8439        }
8440
8441        // check length next
8442        if (end > str.length()) {
8443            end = str.length();
8444        }
8445
8446        // if start is greater than end, return ""
8447        if (start > end) {
8448            return EMPTY;
8449        }
8450
8451        if (start < 0) {
8452            start = 0;
8453        }
8454        if (end < 0) {
8455            end = 0;
8456        }
8457
8458        return str.substring(start, end);
8459    }
8460
8461    /**
8462     * Gets the substring after the first occurrence of a separator.
8463     * The separator is not returned.
8464     *
8465     * <p>A {@code null} string input will return {@code null}.
8466     * An empty ("") string input will return the empty string.
8467     *
8468     * <p>If nothing is found, the empty string is returned.</p>
8469     *
8470     * <pre>
8471     * StringUtils.substringAfter(null, *)      = null
8472     * StringUtils.substringAfter("", *)        = ""
8473     * StringUtils.substringAfter("abc", 'a')   = "bc"
8474     * StringUtils.substringAfter("abcba", 'b') = "cba"
8475     * StringUtils.substringAfter("abc", 'c')   = ""
8476     * StringUtils.substringAfter("abc", 'd')   = ""
8477     * StringUtils.substringAfter(" abc", 32)   = "abc"
8478     * </pre>
8479     *
8480     * @param str  the String to get a substring from, may be null
8481     * @param separator  the character (Unicode code point) to search.
8482     * @return the substring after the first occurrence of the separator,
8483     *  {@code null} if null String input
8484     * @since 3.11
8485     */
8486    public static String substringAfter(final String str, final int separator) {
8487        if (isEmpty(str)) {
8488            return str;
8489        }
8490        final int pos = str.indexOf(separator);
8491        if (pos == INDEX_NOT_FOUND) {
8492            return EMPTY;
8493        }
8494        return str.substring(pos + 1);
8495    }

8497    /**
8498     * Gets the substring after the first occurrence of a separator.
8499     * The separator is not returned.
8500     *
8501     * <p>A {@code null} string input will return {@code null}.
8502     * An empty ("") string input will return the empty string.
8503     * A {@code null} separator will return the empty string if the
8504     * input string is not {@code null}.</p>
8505     *
8506     * <p>If nothing is found, the empty string is returned.</p>
8507     *
8508     * <pre>
8509     * StringUtils.substringAfter(null, *)      = null
8510     * StringUtils.substringAfter("", *)        = ""
8511     * StringUtils.substringAfter(*, null)      = ""
8512     * StringUtils.substringAfter("abc", "a")   = "bc"
8513     * StringUtils.substringAfter("abcba", "b") = "cba"
8514     * StringUtils.substringAfter("abc", "c")   = ""
8515     * StringUtils.substringAfter("abc", "d")   = ""
8516     * StringUtils.substringAfter("abc", "")    = "abc"
8517     * </pre>
8518     *
8519     * @param str  the String to get a substring from, may be null
8520     * @param separator  the String to search for, may be null
8521     * @return the substring after the first occurrence of the separator,
8522     *  {@code null} if null String input
8523     * @since 2.0
8524     */
8525    public static String substringAfter(final String str, final String separator) {
8526        if (isEmpty(str)) {
8527            return str;
8528        }
8529        if (separator == null) {
8530            return EMPTY;
8531        }
8532        final int pos = str.indexOf(separator);
8533        if (pos == INDEX_NOT_FOUND) {
8534            return EMPTY;
8535        }
8536        return str.substring(pos + separator.length());
8537    }

8539    /**
8540     * Gets the substring after the last occurrence of a separator.
8541     * The separator is not returned.
8542     *
8543     * <p>A {@code null} string input will return {@code null}.
8544     * An empty ("") string input will return the empty string.
8545     *
8546     * <p>If nothing is found, the empty string is returned.</p>
8547     *
8548     * <pre>
8549     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast(null, *)      = null
8550     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast("", *)        = ""
8551     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast("abc", 'a')   = "bc"
8552     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast(" bc", 32)    = "bc"
8553     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast("abcba", 'b') = "a"
8554     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast("abc", 'c')   = ""
8555     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast("a", 'a')     = ""
8556     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast("a", 'z')     = ""
8557     * </pre>
8558     *
8559     * @param str  the String to get a substring from, may be null
8560     * @param separator  the character (Unicode code point) to search.
8561     * @return the substring after the last occurrence of the separator,
8562     *  {@code null} if null String input
8563     * @since 3.11
8564     */
8565    public static String substringAfterLast(final String str, final int separator) {
8566        if (isEmpty(str)) {
8567            return str;
8568        }
8569        final int pos = str.lastIndexOf(separator);
8570        if (pos == INDEX_NOT_FOUND || pos == str.length() - 1) {
8571            return EMPTY;
8572        }
8573        return str.substring(pos + 1);
8574    }

8576    /**
8577     * Gets the substring after the last occurrence of a separator.
8578     * The separator is not returned.
8579     *
8580     * <p>A {@code null} string input will return {@code null}.
8581     * An empty ("") string input will return the empty string.
8582     * An empty or {@code null} separator will return the empty string if
8583     * the input string is not {@code null}.</p>
8584     *
8585     * <p>If nothing is found, the empty string is returned.</p>
8586     *
8587     * <pre>
8588     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast(null, *)      = null
8589     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast("", *)        = ""
8590     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast(*, "")        = ""
8591     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast(*, null)      = ""
8592     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast("abc", "a")   = "bc"
8593     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast("abcba", "b") = "a"
8594     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast("abc", "c")   = ""
8595     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast("a", "a")     = ""
8596     * StringUtils.substringAfterLast("a", "z")     = ""
8597     * </pre>
8598     *
8599     * @param str  the String to get a substring from, may be null
8600     * @param separator  the String to search for, may be null
8601     * @return the substring after the last occurrence of the separator,
8602     *  {@code null} if null String input
8603     * @since 2.0
8604     */
8605    public static String substringAfterLast(final String str, final String separator) {
8606        if (isEmpty(str)) {
8607            return str;
8608        }
8609        if (isEmpty(separator)) {
8610            return EMPTY;
8611        }
8612        final int pos = str.lastIndexOf(separator);
8613        if (pos == INDEX_NOT_FOUND || pos == str.length() - separator.length()) {
8614            return EMPTY;
8615        }
8616        return str.substring(pos + separator.length());
8617    }

8619    /**
8620     * Gets the substring before the first occurrence of a separator. The separator is not returned.
8621     *
8622     * <p>
8623     * A {@code null} string input will return {@code null}. An empty ("") string input will return the empty string.
8624     * </p>
8625     *
8626     * <p>
8627     * If nothing is found, the string input is returned.
8628     * </p>
8629     *
8630     * <pre>
8631     * StringUtils.substringBefore(null, *)      = null
8632     * StringUtils.substringBefore("", *)        = ""
8633     * StringUtils.substringBefore("abc", 'a')   = ""
8634     * StringUtils.substringBefore("abcba", 'b') = "a"
8635     * StringUtils.substringBefore("abc", 'c')   = "ab"
8636     * StringUtils.substringBefore("abc", 'd')   = "abc"
8637     * </pre>
8638     *
8639     * @param str the String to get a substring from, may be null
8640     * @param separator the character (Unicode code point) to search.
8641     * @return the substring before the first occurrence of the separator, {@code null} if null String input
8642     * @since 3.12.0
8643     */
8644    public static String substringBefore(final String str, final int separator) {
8645        if (isEmpty(str)) {
8646            return str;
8647        }
8648        final int pos = str.indexOf(separator);
8649        if (pos == INDEX_NOT_FOUND) {
8650            return str;

8652        return str.substring(0, pos);

8654
8655    /**
8656     * Gets the substring before the first occurrence of a separator.
8657     * The separator is not returned.
8658     *
8659     * <p>A {@code null} string input will return {@code null}.
8660     * An empty ("") string input will return the empty string.
8661     * A {@code null} separator will return the input string.</p>
8662     *
8663     * <p>If nothing is found, the string input is returned.</p>
8664     *
8665     * <pre>
8666     * StringUtils.substringBefore(null, *)      = null
8667     * StringUtils.substringBefore("", *)        = ""
8668     * StringUtils.substringBefore("abc", "a")   = ""
8669     * StringUtils.substringBefore("abcba", "b") = "a"
8670     * StringUtils.substringBefore("abc", "c")   = "ab"
8671     * StringUtils.substringBefore("abc", "d")   = "abc"
8672     * StringUtils.substringBefore("abc", "")    = ""
8673     * StringUtils.substringBefore("abc", null)  = "abc"
8674     * </pre>
8675     *
8676     * @param str  the String to get a substring from, may be null
8677     * @param separator  the String to search for, may be null
8678     * @return the substring before the first occurrence of the separator,
8679     *  {@code null} if null String input
8680     * @since 2.0
8681     */
8682    public static String substringBefore(final String str, final String separator) {
8683        if (isEmpty(str) || separator == null) {
8684            return str;
8685        }
8686        if (separator.isEmpty()) {
8687            return EMPTY;
8688        }
8689        final int pos = str.indexOf(separator);
8690        if (pos == INDEX_NOT_FOUND) {
8691            return str;
8692        }
8693        return str.substring(0, pos);
8694    }
8695
8696    /**
8697     * Gets the substring before the last occurrence of a separator.
8698     * The separator is not returned.
8699     *
8700     * <p>A {@code null} string input will return {@code null}.
8701     * An empty ("") string input will return the empty string.
8702     * An empty or {@code null} separator will return the input string.</p>
8703     *
8704     * <p>If nothing is found, the string input is returned.</p>
8705     *
8706     * <pre>
8707     * StringUtils.substringBeforeLast(null, *)      = null
8708     * StringUtils.substringBeforeLast("", *)        = ""
8709     * StringUtils.substringBeforeLast("abcba", "b") = "abc"
8710     * StringUtils.substringBeforeLast("abc", "c")   = "ab"
8711     * StringUtils.substringBeforeLast("a", "a")     = ""
8712     * StringUtils.substringBeforeLast("a", "z")     = "a"
8713     * StringUtils.substringBeforeLast("a", null)    = "a"
8714     * StringUtils.substringBeforeLast("a", "")      = "a"
8715     * </pre>
8716     *
8717     * @param str  the String to get a substring from, may be null
8718     * @param separator  the String to search for, may be null
8719     * @return the substring before the last occurrence of the separator,
8720     *  {@code null} if null String input
8721     * @since 2.0
8722     */
8723    public static String substringBeforeLast(final String str, final String separator) {
8724        if (isEmpty(str) || isEmpty(separator)) {
8725            return str;
8726        }
8727        final int pos = str.lastIndexOf(separator);
8728        if (pos == INDEX_NOT_FOUND) {
8729            return str;
8730        }
8731        return str.substring(0, pos);
8732    }
8733
8734    /**
8735     * Gets the String that is nested in between two instances of the
8736     * same String.
8737     *
8738     * <p>A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.
8739     * A {@code null} tag returns {@code null}.</p>
8740     *
8741     * <pre>
8742     * StringUtils.substringBetween(null, *)            = null
8743     * StringUtils.substringBetween("", "")             = ""
8744     * StringUtils.substringBetween("", "tag")          = null
8745     * StringUtils.substringBetween("tagabctag", null)  = null
8746     * StringUtils.substringBetween("tagabctag", "")    = ""
8747     * StringUtils.substringBetween("tagabctag", "tag") = "abc"
8748     * </pre>
8749     *
8750     * @param str  the String containing the substring, may be null
8751     * @param tag  the String before and after the substring, may be null
8752     * @return the substring, {@code null} if no match
8753     * @since 2.0
8754     */
8755    public static String substringBetween(final String str, final String tag) {
8756        return substringBetween(str, tag, tag);
8757    }
8758
8759    /**
8760     * Gets the String that is nested in between two Strings.
8761     * Only the first match is returned.
8762     *
8763     * <p>A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.
8764     * A {@code null} open/close returns {@code null} (no match).
8765     * An empty ("") open and close returns an empty string.</p>
8766     *
8767     * <pre>
8768     * StringUtils.substringBetween("wx[b]yz", "[", "]") = "b"
8769     * StringUtils.substringBetween(null, *, *)          = null
8770     * StringUtils.substringBetween(*, null, *)          = null
8771     * StringUtils.substringBetween(*, *, null)          = null
8772     * StringUtils.substringBetween("", "", "")          = ""
8773     * StringUtils.substringBetween("", "", "]")         = null
8774     * StringUtils.substringBetween("", "[", "]")        = null
8775     * StringUtils.substringBetween("yabcz", "", "")     = ""
8776     * StringUtils.substringBetween("yabcz", "y", "z")   = "abc"
8777     * StringUtils.substringBetween("yabczyabcz", "y", "z")   = "abc"
8778     * </pre>
8779     *
8780     * @param str  the String containing the substring, may be null
8781     * @param open  the String before the substring, may be null
8782     * @param close  the String after the substring, may be null
8783     * @return the substring, {@code null} if no match
8784     * @since 2.0
8785     */
8786    public static String substringBetween(final String str, final String open, final String close) {
8787        if (!ObjectUtils.allNotNull(str, open, close)) {
8788            return null;
8789        }
8790        final int start = str.indexOf(open);
8791        if (start != INDEX_NOT_FOUND) {
8792            final int end = str.indexOf(close, start + open.length());
8793            if (end != INDEX_NOT_FOUND) {
8794                return str.substring(start + open.length(), end);
8795            }
8796        }
8797        return null;
8798    }
8799
8800    /**
8801     * Searches a String for substrings delimited by a start and end tag,
8802     * returning all matching substrings in an array.
8803     *
8804     * <p>A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.
8805     * A {@code null} open/close returns {@code null} (no match).
8806     * An empty ("") open/close returns {@code null} (no match).</p>
8807     *
8808     * <pre>
8809     * StringUtils.substringsBetween("[a][b][c]", "[", "]") = ["a","b","c"]
8810     * StringUtils.substringsBetween(null, *, *)            = null
8811     * StringUtils.substringsBetween(*, null, *)            = null
8812     * StringUtils.substringsBetween(*, *, null)            = null
8813     * StringUtils.substringsBetween("", "[", "]")          = []
8814     * </pre>
8815     *
8816     * @param str  the String containing the substrings, null returns null, empty returns empty
8817     * @param open  the String identifying the start of the substring, empty returns null
8818     * @param close  the String identifying the end of the substring, empty returns null
8819     * @return a String Array of substrings, or {@code null} if no match
8820     * @since 2.3
8821     */
8822    public static String[] substringsBetween(final String str, final String open, final String close) {
8823        if (str == null || isEmpty(open) || isEmpty(close)) {
8824            return null;
8825        }
8826        final int strLen = str.length();
8827        if (strLen == 0) {
8828            return ArrayUtils.EMPTY_STRING_ARRAY;
8829        }
8830        final int closeLen = close.length();
8831        final int openLen = open.length();
8832        final List<String> list = new ArrayList<>();
8833        int pos = 0;
8834        while (pos < strLen - closeLen) {
8835            int start = str.indexOf(open, pos);
8836            if (start < 0) {
8837                break;
8838            }
8839            start += openLen;
8840            final int end = str.indexOf(close, start);
8841            if (end < 0) {
8842                break;
8843            }
8844            list.add(str.substring(start, end));
8845            pos = end + closeLen;
8846        }
8847        if (list.isEmpty()) {
8848            return null;
8849        }
8850        return list.toArray(ArrayUtils.EMPTY_STRING_ARRAY);
8851    }
8852
8853    /**
8854     * Swaps the case of a String changing upper and title case to
8855     * lower case, and lower case to upper case.
8856     *
8857     * <ul>
8858     *  <li>Upper case character converts to Lower case</li>
8859     *  <li>Title case character converts to Lower case</li>
8860     *  <li>Lower case character converts to Upper case</li>
8861     * </ul>
8862     *
8863     * <p>For a word based algorithm, see {@link org.apache.commons.text.WordUtils#swapCase(String)}.
8864     * A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.</p>
8865     *
8866     * <pre>
8867     * StringUtils.swapCase(null)                 = null
8868     * StringUtils.swapCase("")                   = ""
8869     * StringUtils.swapCase("The dog has a BONE") = "tHE DOG HAS A bone"
8870     * </pre>
8871     *
8872     * <p>NOTE: This method changed in Lang version 2.0.
8873     * It no longer performs a word based algorithm.
8874     * If you only use ASCII, you will notice no change.
8875     * That functionality is available in org.apache.commons.lang3.text.WordUtils.</p>
8876     *
8877     * @param str  the String to swap case, may be null
8878     * @return the changed String, {@code null} if null String input
8879     */
8880    public static String swapCase(final String str) {
8881        if (isEmpty(str)) {
8882            return str;
8883        }
8884
8885        final int strLen = str.length();
8886        final int[] newCodePoints = new int[strLen]; // cannot be longer than the char array
8887        int outOffset = 0;
8888        for (int i = 0; i < strLen; ) {
8889            final int oldCodepoint = str.codePointAt(i);
8890            final int newCodePoint;
8891            if (Character.isUpperCase(oldCodepoint) || Character.isTitleCase(oldCodepoint)) {
8892                newCodePoint = Character.toLowerCase(oldCodepoint);
8893            } else if (Character.isLowerCase(oldCodepoint)) {
8894                newCodePoint = Character.toUpperCase(oldCodepoint);
8895            } else {
8896                newCodePoint = oldCodepoint;
8897            }
8898            newCodePoints[outOffset++] = newCodePoint;
8899            i += Character.charCount(newCodePoint);
8900         }
8901        return new String(newCodePoints, 0, outOffset);
8902    }
8903
8904    /**
8905     * Converts a {@link CharSequence} into an array of code points.
8906     *
8907     * <p>Valid pairs of surrogate code units will be converted into a single supplementary
8908     * code point. Isolated surrogate code units (i.e. a high surrogate not followed by a low surrogate or
8909     * a low surrogate not preceded by a high surrogate) will be returned as-is.</p>
8910     *
8911     * <pre>
8912     * StringUtils.toCodePoints(null)   =  null
8913     * StringUtils.toCodePoints("")     =  []  // empty array
8914     * </pre>
8915     *
8916     * @param cs the character sequence to convert
8917     * @return an array of code points
8918     * @since 3.6
8919     */
8920    public static int[] toCodePoints(final CharSequence cs) {
8921        if (cs == null) {
8922            return null;
8923        }
8924        if (cs.length() == 0) {
8925            return ArrayUtils.EMPTY_INT_ARRAY;
8926        }
8927
8928        final String s = cs.toString();
8929        final int[] result = new int[s.codePointCount(0, s.length())];
8930        int index = 0;
8931        for (int i = 0; i < result.length; i++) {
8932            result[i] = s.codePointAt(index);
8933            index += Character.charCount(result[i]);
8934        }
8935        return result;
8936    }

9001    /**
9002     * Removes control characters (char &lt;= 32) from both
9003     * ends of this String, handling {@code null} by returning
9004     * {@code null}.
9005     *
9006     * <p>The String is trimmed using {@link String#trim()}.
9007     * Trim removes start and end characters &lt;= 32.
9008     * To strip whitespace use {@link #strip(String)}.</p>
9009     *
9010     * <p>To trim your choice of characters, use the
9011     * {@link #strip(String, String)} methods.</p>
9012     *
9013     * <pre>
9014     * StringUtils.trim(null)          = null
9015     * StringUtils.trim("")            = ""
9016     * StringUtils.trim("     ")       = ""
9017     * StringUtils.trim("abc")         = "abc"
9018     * StringUtils.trim("    abc    ") = "abc"
9019     * </pre>
9020     *
9021     * @param str  the String to be trimmed, may be null
9022     * @return the trimmed string, {@code null} if null String input
9023     */
9024    public static String trim(final String str) {
9025        return str == null ? null : str.trim();
9026    }

9028    /**
9029     * Removes control characters (char &lt;= 32) from both
9030     * ends of this String returning an empty String ("") if the String
9031     * is empty ("") after the trim or if it is {@code null}.
9032     *
9033     * <p>The String is trimmed using {@link String#trim()}.
9034     * Trim removes start and end characters &lt;= 32.
9035     * To strip whitespace use {@link #stripToEmpty(String)}.
9036     *
9037     * <pre>
9038     * StringUtils.trimToEmpty(null)          = ""
9039     * StringUtils.trimToEmpty("")            = ""
9040     * StringUtils.trimToEmpty("     ")       = ""
9041     * StringUtils.trimToEmpty("abc")         = "abc"
9042     * StringUtils.trimToEmpty("    abc    ") = "abc"
9043     * </pre>
9044     *
9045     * @param str  the String to be trimmed, may be null
9046     * @return the trimmed String, or an empty String if {@code null} input
9047     * @since 2.0
9048     */
9049    public static String trimToEmpty(final String str) {
9050        return str == null ? EMPTY : str.trim();
9051    }

9053    /**
9054     * Removes control characters (char &lt;= 32) from both
9055     * ends of this String returning {@code null} if the String is
9056     * empty ("") after the trim or if it is {@code null}.
9057     *
9058     * <p>The String is trimmed using {@link String#trim()}.
9059     * Trim removes start and end characters &lt;= 32.
9060     * To strip whitespace use {@link #stripToNull(String)}.
9061     *
9062     * <pre>
9063     * StringUtils.trimToNull(null)          = null
9064     * StringUtils.trimToNull("")            = null
9065     * StringUtils.trimToNull("     ")       = null
9066     * StringUtils.trimToNull("abc")         = "abc"
9067     * StringUtils.trimToNull("    abc    ") = "abc"
9068     * </pre>
9069     *
9070     * @param str  the String to be trimmed, may be null
9071     * @return the trimmed String,
9072     *  {@code null} if only chars &lt;= 32, empty or null String input
9073     * @since 2.0
9074     */
9075    public static String trimToNull(final String str) {
9076        final String ts = trim(str);
9077        return isEmpty(ts) ? null : ts;
9078    }

9080    /**
9081     * Truncates a String. This will turn
9082     * "Now is the time for all good men" into "Now is the time for".
9083     *
9084     * <p>Specifically:</p>
9085     * <ul>
9086     *   <li>If {@code str} is less than {@code maxWidth} characters
9087     *       long, return it.</li>
9088     *   <li>Else truncate it to {@code substring(str, 0, maxWidth)}.</li>
9089     *   <li>If {@code maxWidth} is less than {@code 0}, throw an
9090     *       {@link IllegalArgumentException}.</li>
9091     *   <li>In no case will it return a String of length greater than
9092     *       {@code maxWidth}.</li>
9093     * </ul>
9094     *
9095     * <pre>
9096     * StringUtils.truncate(null, 0)       = null
9097     * StringUtils.truncate(null, 2)       = null
9098     * StringUtils.truncate("", 4)         = ""
9099     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefg", 4)  = "abcd"
9100     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefg", 6)  = "abcdef"
9101     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefg", 7)  = "abcdefg"
9102     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefg", 8)  = "abcdefg"
9103     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefg", -1) = throws an IllegalArgumentException
9104     * </pre>
9105     *
9106     * @param str  the String to truncate, may be null
9107     * @param maxWidth  maximum length of result String, must be positive
9108     * @return truncated String, {@code null} if null String input
9109     * @throws IllegalArgumentException If {@code maxWidth} is less than {@code 0}
9110     * @since 3.5
9111     */
9112    public static String truncate(final String str, final int maxWidth) {
9113        return truncate(str, 0, maxWidth);
9114    }
9115
9116    /**
9117     * Truncates a String. This will turn
9118     * "Now is the time for all good men" into "is the time for all".
9119     *
9120     * <p>Works like {@code truncate(String, int)}, but allows you to specify
9121     * a "left edge" offset.
9122     *
9123     * <p>Specifically:</p>
9124     * <ul>
9125     *   <li>If {@code str} is less than {@code maxWidth} characters
9126     *       long, return it.</li>
9127     *   <li>Else truncate it to {@code substring(str, offset, maxWidth)}.</li>
9128     *   <li>If {@code maxWidth} is less than {@code 0}, throw an
9129     *       {@link IllegalArgumentException}.</li>
9130     *   <li>If {@code offset} is less than {@code 0}, throw an
9131     *       {@link IllegalArgumentException}.</li>
9132     *   <li>In no case will it return a String of length greater than
9133     *       {@code maxWidth}.</li>
9134     * </ul>
9135     *
9136     * <pre>
9137     * StringUtils.truncate(null, 0, 0) = null
9138     * StringUtils.truncate(null, 2, 4) = null
9139     * StringUtils.truncate("", 0, 10) = ""
9140     * StringUtils.truncate("", 2, 10) = ""
9141     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghij", 0, 3) = "abc"
9142     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghij", 5, 6) = "fghij"
9143     * StringUtils.truncate("raspberry peach", 10, 15) = "peach"
9144     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 0, 10) = "abcdefghij"
9145     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", -1, 10) = throws an IllegalArgumentException
9146     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", Integer.MIN_VALUE, 10) = throws an IllegalArgumentException
9147     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", Integer.MIN_VALUE, Integer.MAX_VALUE) = throws an IllegalArgumentException
9148     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 0, Integer.MAX_VALUE) = "abcdefghijklmno"
9149     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 1, 10) = "bcdefghijk"
9150     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 2, 10) = "cdefghijkl"
9151     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 3, 10) = "defghijklm"
9152     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 4, 10) = "efghijklmn"
9153     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 5, 10) = "fghijklmno"
9154     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 5, 5) = "fghij"
9155     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 5, 3) = "fgh"
9156     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 10, 3) = "klm"
9157     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 10, Integer.MAX_VALUE) = "klmno"
9158     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 13, 1) = "n"
9159     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 13, Integer.MAX_VALUE) = "no"
9160     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 14, 1) = "o"
9161     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 14, Integer.MAX_VALUE) = "o"
9162     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 15, 1) = ""
9163     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", 15, Integer.MAX_VALUE) = ""
9164     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghijklmno", Integer.MAX_VALUE, Integer.MAX_VALUE) = ""
9165     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghij", 3, -1) = throws an IllegalArgumentException
9166     * StringUtils.truncate("abcdefghij", -2, 4) = throws an IllegalArgumentException
9167     * </pre>
9168     *
9169     * @param str  the String to truncate, may be null
9170     * @param offset  left edge of source String
9171     * @param maxWidth  maximum length of result String, must be positive
9172     * @return truncated String, {@code null} if null String input
9173     * @throws IllegalArgumentException If {@code offset} or {@code maxWidth} is less than {@code 0}
9174     * @since 3.5
9175     */
9176    public static String truncate(final String str, final int offset, final int maxWidth) {
9177        if (offset < 0) {
9178            throw new IllegalArgumentException("offset cannot be negative");
9179        }
9180        if (maxWidth < 0) {
9181            throw new IllegalArgumentException("maxWith cannot be negative");
9182        }
9183        if (str == null) {
9184            return null;
9185        }
9186        if (offset > str.length()) {
9187            return EMPTY;
9188        }
9189        if (str.length() > maxWidth) {
9190            final int ix = Math.min(offset + maxWidth, str.length());
9191            return str.substring(offset, ix);
9192        }
9193        return str.substring(offset);
9194    }
9195
9196    /**
9197     * Uncapitalizes a String, changing the first character to lower case as
9198     * per {@link Character#toLowerCase(int)}. No other characters are changed.
9199     *
9200     * <p>For a word based algorithm, see {@link org.apache.commons.text.WordUtils#uncapitalize(String)}.
9201     * A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.</p>
9202     *
9203     * <pre>
9204     * StringUtils.uncapitalize(null)  = null
9205     * StringUtils.uncapitalize("")    = ""
9206     * StringUtils.uncapitalize("cat") = "cat"
9207     * StringUtils.uncapitalize("Cat") = "cat"
9208     * StringUtils.uncapitalize("CAT") = "cAT"
9209     * </pre>
9210     *
9211     * @param str the String to uncapitalize, may be null
9212     * @return the uncapitalized String, {@code null} if null String input
9213     * @see org.apache.commons.text.WordUtils#uncapitalize(String)
9214     * @see #capitalize(String)
9215     * @since 2.0
9216     */
9217    public static String uncapitalize(final String str) {
9218        final int strLen = length(str);
9219        if (strLen == 0) {
9220            return str;
9221        }
9222
9223        final int firstCodePoint = str.codePointAt(0);
9224        final int newCodePoint = Character.toLowerCase(firstCodePoint);
9225        if (firstCodePoint == newCodePoint) {
9226            // already capitalized
9227            return str;
9228        }
9229
9230        final int[] newCodePoints = new int[strLen]; // cannot be longer than the char array
9231        int outOffset = 0;
9232        newCodePoints[outOffset++] = newCodePoint; // copy the first code point
9233        for (int inOffset = Character.charCount(firstCodePoint); inOffset < strLen; ) {
9234            final int codePoint = str.codePointAt(inOffset);
9235            newCodePoints[outOffset++] = codePoint; // copy the remaining ones
9236            inOffset += Character.charCount(codePoint);
9237         }
9238        return new String(newCodePoints, 0, outOffset);
9239    }
9240
9241    /**
9242     * Unwraps a given string from a character.
9243     *
9244     * <pre>
9245     * StringUtils.unwrap(null, null)         = null
9246     * StringUtils.unwrap(null, '\0')         = null
9247     * StringUtils.unwrap(null, '1')          = null
9248     * StringUtils.unwrap("a", 'a')           = "a"
9249     * StringUtils.unwrap("aa", 'a')           = ""
9250     * StringUtils.unwrap("\'abc\'", '\'')    = "abc"
9251     * StringUtils.unwrap("AABabcBAA", 'A')   = "ABabcBA"
9252     * StringUtils.unwrap("A", '#')           = "A"
9253     * StringUtils.unwrap("#A", '#')          = "#A"
9254     * StringUtils.unwrap("A#", '#')          = "A#"
9255     * </pre>
9256     *
9257     * @param str
9258     *          the String to be unwrapped, can be null
9259     * @param wrapChar
9260     *          the character used to unwrap
9261     * @return unwrapped String or the original string
9262     *          if it is not quoted properly with the wrapChar
9263     * @since 3.6
9264     */
9265    public static String unwrap(final String str, final char wrapChar) {
9266        if (isEmpty(str) || wrapChar == CharUtils.NUL || str.length() == 1) {
9267            return str;
9268        }
9269
9270        if (str.charAt(0) == wrapChar && str.charAt(str.length() - 1) == wrapChar) {
9271            final int startIndex = 0;
9272            final int endIndex = str.length() - 1;
9273
9274            return str.substring(startIndex + 1, endIndex);
9275        }
9276
9277        return str;
9278    }
9279
9280    /**
9281     * Unwraps a given string from another string.
9282     *
9283     * <pre>
9284     * StringUtils.unwrap(null, null)         = null
9285     * StringUtils.unwrap(null, "")           = null
9286     * StringUtils.unwrap(null, "1")          = null
9287     * StringUtils.unwrap("a", "a")           = "a"
9288     * StringUtils.unwrap("aa", "a")          = ""
9289     * StringUtils.unwrap("\'abc\'", "\'")    = "abc"
9290     * StringUtils.unwrap("\"abc\"", "\"")    = "abc"
9291     * StringUtils.unwrap("AABabcBAA", "AA")  = "BabcB"
9292     * StringUtils.unwrap("A", "#")           = "A"
9293     * StringUtils.unwrap("#A", "#")          = "#A"
9294     * StringUtils.unwrap("A#", "#")          = "A#"
9295     * </pre>
9296     *
9297     * @param str
9298     *          the String to be unwrapped, can be null
9299     * @param wrapToken
9300     *          the String used to unwrap
9301     * @return unwrapped String or the original string
9302     *          if it is not quoted properly with the wrapToken
9303     * @since 3.6
9304     */
9305    public static String unwrap(final String str, final String wrapToken) {
9306        if (isEmpty(str) || isEmpty(wrapToken) || str.length() < 2 * wrapToken.length()) {
9307            return str;
9308        }
9309
9310        if (startsWith(str, wrapToken) && endsWith(str, wrapToken)) {
9311            return str.substring(wrapToken.length(), str.lastIndexOf(wrapToken));
9312        }
9313
9314        return str;
9315    }
9316
9317    /**
9318     * Converts a String to upper case as per {@link String#toUpperCase()}.
9319     *
9320     * <p>A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.</p>
9321     *
9322     * <pre>
9323     * StringUtils.upperCase(null)  = null
9324     * StringUtils.upperCase("")    = ""
9325     * StringUtils.upperCase("aBc") = "ABC"
9326     * </pre>
9327     *
9328     * <p><strong>Note:</strong> As described in the documentation for {@link String#toUpperCase()},
9329     * the result of this method is affected by the current locale.
9330     * For platform-independent case transformations, the method {@link #upperCase(String, Locale)}
9331     * should be used with a specific locale (e.g. {@link Locale#ENGLISH}).</p>
9332     *
9333     * @param str  the String to upper case, may be null
9334     * @return the upper-cased String, {@code null} if null String input
9335     */
9336    public static String upperCase(final String str) {
9337        if (str == null) {
9338            return null;
9339        }
9340        return str.toUpperCase();
9341    }
9342
9343    /**
9344     * Converts a String to upper case as per {@link String#toUpperCase(Locale)}.
9345     *
9346     * <p>A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.</p>
9347     *
9348     * <pre>
9349     * StringUtils.upperCase(null, Locale.ENGLISH)  = null
9350     * StringUtils.upperCase("", Locale.ENGLISH)    = ""
9351     * StringUtils.upperCase("aBc", Locale.ENGLISH) = "ABC"
9352     * </pre>
9353     *
9354     * @param str  the String to upper case, may be null
9355     * @param locale  the locale that defines the case transformation rules, must not be null
9356     * @return the upper-cased String, {@code null} if null String input
9357     * @since 2.5
9358     */
9359    public static String upperCase(final String str, final Locale locale) {
9360        if (str == null) {
9361            return null;
9362        }
9363        return str.toUpperCase(LocaleUtils.toLocale(locale));
9364    }

9366    /**
9367     * Returns the string representation of the {@code char} array or null.
9368     *
9369     * @param value the character array.
9370     * @return a String or null
9371     * @see String#valueOf(char[])
9372     * @since 3.9
9373     */
9374    public static String valueOf(final char[] value) {
9375        return value == null ? null : String.valueOf(value);
9376    }
9377
9378    /**
9379     * Wraps a string with a char.
9380     *
9381     * <pre>
9382     * StringUtils.wrap(null, *)        = null
9383     * StringUtils.wrap("", *)          = ""
9384     * StringUtils.wrap("ab", '\0')     = "ab"
9385     * StringUtils.wrap("ab", 'x')      = "xabx"
9386     * StringUtils.wrap("ab", '\'')     = "'ab'"
9387     * StringUtils.wrap("\"ab\"", '\"') = "\"\"ab\"\""
9388     * </pre>
9389     *
9390     * @param str
9391     *            the string to be wrapped, may be {@code null}
9392     * @param wrapWith
9393     *            the char that will wrap {@code str}
9394     * @return the wrapped string, or {@code null} if {@code str==null}
9395     * @since 3.4
9396     */
9397    public static String wrap(final String str, final char wrapWith) {
9398
9399        if (isEmpty(str) || wrapWith == CharUtils.NUL) {
9400            return str;
9401        }
9402
9403        return wrapWith + str + wrapWith;
9404    }
9405
9406    /**
9407     * Wraps a String with another String.
9408     *
9409     * <p>
9410     * A {@code null} input String returns {@code null}.
9411     * </p>
9412     *
9413     * <pre>
9414     * StringUtils.wrap(null, *)         = null
9415     * StringUtils.wrap("", *)           = ""
9416     * StringUtils.wrap("ab", null)      = "ab"
9417     * StringUtils.wrap("ab", "x")       = "xabx"
9418     * StringUtils.wrap("ab", "\"")      = "\"ab\""
9419     * StringUtils.wrap("\"ab\"", "\"")  = "\"\"ab\"\""
9420     * StringUtils.wrap("ab", "'")       = "'ab'"
9421     * StringUtils.wrap("'abcd'", "'")   = "''abcd''"
9422     * StringUtils.wrap("\"abcd\"", "'") = "'\"abcd\"'"
9423     * StringUtils.wrap("'abcd'", "\"")  = "\"'abcd'\""
9424     * </pre>
9425     *
9426     * @param str
9427     *            the String to be wrapper, may be null
9428     * @param wrapWith
9429     *            the String that will wrap str
9430     * @return wrapped String, {@code null} if null String input
9431     * @since 3.4
9432     */
9433    public static String wrap(final String str, final String wrapWith) {
9434
9435        if (isEmpty(str) || isEmpty(wrapWith)) {
9436            return str;
9437        }
9438
9439        return wrapWith.concat(str).concat(wrapWith);
9440    }
9441
9442    /**
9443     * Wraps a string with a char if that char is missing from the start or end of the given string.
9444     *
9445     * <p>A new {@link String} will not be created if {@code str} is already wrapped.</p>
9446     *
9447     * <pre>
9448     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing(null, *)        = null
9449     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("", *)          = ""
9450     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("ab", '\0')     = "ab"
9451     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("ab", 'x')      = "xabx"
9452     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("ab", '\'')     = "'ab'"
9453     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("\"ab\"", '\"') = "\"ab\""
9454     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("/", '/')  = "/"
9455     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("a/b/c", '/')  = "/a/b/c/"
9456     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("/a/b/c", '/')  = "/a/b/c/"
9457     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("a/b/c/", '/')  = "/a/b/c/"
9458     * </pre>
9459     *
9460     * @param str
9461     *            the string to be wrapped, may be {@code null}
9462     * @param wrapWith
9463     *            the char that will wrap {@code str}
9464     * @return the wrapped string, or {@code null} if {@code str==null}
9465     * @since 3.5
9466     */
9467    public static String wrapIfMissing(final String str, final char wrapWith) {
9468        if (isEmpty(str) || wrapWith == CharUtils.NUL) {
9469            return str;
9470        }
9471        final boolean wrapStart = str.charAt(0) != wrapWith;
9472        final boolean wrapEnd = str.charAt(str.length() - 1) != wrapWith;
9473        if (!wrapStart && !wrapEnd) {
9474            return str;
9475        }
9476
9477        final StringBuilder builder = new StringBuilder(str.length() + 2);
9478        if (wrapStart) {
9479            builder.append(wrapWith);
9480        }
9481        builder.append(str);
9482        if (wrapEnd) {
9483            builder.append(wrapWith);
9484        }
9485        return builder.toString();
9486    }
9487
9488    /**
9489     * Wraps a string with a string if that string is missing from the start or end of the given string.
9490     *
9491     * <p>A new {@link String} will not be created if {@code str} is already wrapped.</p>
9492     *
9493     * <pre>
9494     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing(null, *)         = null
9495     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("", *)           = ""
9496     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("ab", null)      = "ab"
9497     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("ab", "x")       = "xabx"
9498     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("ab", "\"")      = "\"ab\""
9499     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("\"ab\"", "\"")  = "\"ab\""
9500     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("ab", "'")       = "'ab'"
9501     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("'abcd'", "'")   = "'abcd'"
9502     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("\"abcd\"", "'") = "'\"abcd\"'"
9503     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("'abcd'", "\"")  = "\"'abcd'\""
9504     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("/", "/")  = "/"
9505     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("a/b/c", "/")  = "/a/b/c/"
9506     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("/a/b/c", "/")  = "/a/b/c/"
9507     * StringUtils.wrapIfMissing("a/b/c/", "/")  = "/a/b/c/"
9508     * </pre>
9509     *
9510     * @param str
9511     *            the string to be wrapped, may be {@code null}
9512     * @param wrapWith
9513     *            the string that will wrap {@code str}
9514     * @return the wrapped string, or {@code null} if {@code str==null}
9515     * @since 3.5
9516     */
9517    public static String wrapIfMissing(final String str, final String wrapWith) {
9518        if (isEmpty(str) || isEmpty(wrapWith)) {
9519            return str;
9520        }
9521
9522        final boolean wrapStart = !str.startsWith(wrapWith);
9523        final boolean wrapEnd = !str.endsWith(wrapWith);
9524        if (!wrapStart && !wrapEnd) {
9525            return str;
9526        }
9527
9528        final StringBuilder builder = new StringBuilder(str.length() + wrapWith.length() + wrapWith.length());
9529        if (wrapStart) {
9530            builder.append(wrapWith);
9531        }
9532        builder.append(str);
9533        if (wrapEnd) {
9534            builder.append(wrapWith);
9535        }
9536        return builder.toString();
9537    }

9539    /**
9540     * {@link StringUtils} instances should NOT be constructed in
9541     * standard programming. Instead, the class should be used as
9542     * {@code StringUtils.trim(" foo ");}.
9543     *
9544     * <p>This constructor is public to permit tools that require a JavaBean
9545     * instance to operate.</p>
9546     */
9547    public StringUtils() {
9548    }
